<Author>JChua
<Content>Langham Suite 3620. Having been to Hong Kong for the past 30 years and stayed at numerous 3, 4 and 5 star hotels, we chose this hotel based mainly on Tripadvisor's top ratings - and we were happy that we did so for a 2 night stay, from 9 to 11 April. Booked their Langham suite and requested for a higher floor room with good views of the Victoria Harbour. Upon check in at 7pm, we were given room 3620, on the same level as its Club Lounge - very convenient to drop by the Lounge for both checking in and out. View wise, yes, it was quite good too but the Victoria Harbour was a far distance away (nothing as compared to the Hotel Intercontinental and Hotel Peninsula). Though we knew from its website that the suite was 600 square feet in total area, our first impression was - is this really 600 square feet? Though in reality, the suite had appeared smaller than its website pictures, the suite was, nevertheless, cosy and very comfy, good enough for a few nights stay. There are two toilets in the suite - one main one with both shower and large tub while the other merely has a toilet and a single sink. There is also a kitchennette with a coffee maker, a water kettle, mini bar with free ice creams!, bread toaster etcChocolate coated biscuits were also placed in our suite upon arrival, a well appreciated gesture after a long day in Guangzhou! Two bottles of distilled water were also replenished daily in the main toilet. Besides an easy to use safe, there is also an iron and ironing board, two flat screen TVs (of the Haier brand that has somewhat poorer resolution), 2 seater sofa (very hard and uncomfortable though!), single seater and a small dinning table with two chairs for small meals. Our separated bedroom (with a lock for extra security) comes with two twin beds, as requested. The beds were, in our opinions, comfy enough but not of the Westin quality. And each person were given 3 different types of pillows (even with a small bolster, very rare in hotels!). However, all the pillows were too soft for us to provide enough neck support ....resulting in us having neck strain the next morning. Breakfast was either at the Club Lounge (nice Western varieties but somewhat limited in range) or at the Restaurant on Lobby level. We opted for the latter cos it provided a much wider range, which includes dim sum (though its quality were not up to par with those served in HK restaurants and cafes). On the second day, we ''sacrificed'' breakfasts at the Hotel totally and had good dim sum at a nearby Restuarant on Nathan Road (the name is Dou Heung, quite good quality I must say). The roof top swimming pool is a sight to behold, really. Went for an early morning swim and had a memorable time there. The only complaint was, being an open air pool on such a high rise building, it can be quite cold and windy in the mornings.  Our only three glitches here were - 1. on the first day of our stay, our room was not made up even though we were out at 8am and back by 1.30pm 2. even after asking for harder pillows on the phone, they never seem to show up ...? 3. the shopping and local area of Mongkok only offers low to mid range shopping, as higher end brands are almost located on the Hong Kong island side. Though Central was only 5 MTR stops away (a 10 minutes ride), do beware of pickpockets while in the train and while moving up and down the narrow escalator ... My husband's hind trousers pocket were cut open, but luckily, nothing was taken. Lastly, having asked to see the next higher suite category, the Harbour suites (was told that there were only 3 such suites in the hotel), I felt we were glad we didn't opt for that suite category - being at only HK$1,000 more per night (Good value for the extra space), it offers 800 square feet of space with an extra big bathroom, changing room and a small study room. However, the views were nothing as compared to our Langham suite! All in all, we had a wonderful stay at this hotel. Would return to the Langham suite or Residence suite (the same 600 square feet at the same price but with a bigger kitchennette) again.  
<Date>Apr 14, 2008

<Author>Happy95

<Author>JohnEO
<Content>excellent hotel, but small rooms - even smaller bathrooms This was one of two hotels we stayed at in HK, the other being the Novatel Citygates on Lantau Island, near the airport. In many ways, this is an excellent hotel, but it has one major drawback: the rooms are small, and the bathroom is even smaller. For this reason alone, the Novatel was better.Transport to the hotel from the airport is a breeze: go straight to the shuttle bus booths to the right after you come out of arrivals. Langham has a booth (There are two Langham hotels in HK.) The excellent shuttle bus to the airport is 130 HK$ and the service is excellent. (By Mercedes limo, it鈥檚 550 HK$). The sky-blue coated staff give you a sticker. When the bus is ready, they whisk you and your luggage downstairs to the bus. The trip takes about an hour depending on traffic and crosses the famous Tsing Ma Bridge (the world鈥檚 longest road and rail suspension bridge!). You arrive at what looks like a mall in downtown Kowloon, in the Mong Tok district (excellent for shopping and local markets.)The foyer is plush. Check-in was efficient and the staff friendly and welcoming. It鈥檚 when you get to your room that you are disappointed. We reserved a de luxe room on the net, which we thought would be OK. It was not. We were offered a larger room at check-in (First clue) for an additional 700+ HK$, including internet and executive club access. The room is cramped, the bed a tad hard, and the bathroom small. The bathroom is actually a glass box. (The bellman helpfully shows you the blind between the bathroom and the bedroom that you pull down if you don鈥檛 want to watch your partner showering or whatever!) The washbasin and surround is glass, so you need to keep your wits about placing items in the bathroom. The closet is also small but there is a usefully large safe.The hotel has a superb restaurant with excellent Chinese menus and excellent service, and good wine list (Take a coat or sweater to counter HK鈥檚 Arctic AC). Breakfast, which is excellent, comes at 385 HK$ for two. As elsewhere in Asia, except Japan, internet is not free 鈥?although there is a computer suite, with free access, on the third floor. The hotel staff is friendly, helpful, and numerous. The concierge staff will provide you with helpful advice on places to visit and how to get there. As with other hotels in HK, the hotel is connected to a huge mall and MTR (rapid transit) station. Even so, we will probably use the Peninsula or the Shangri-la (on Hong Island Island), if we return to Hong Kong.One really great deal at the hotel is their 1-hour free evening tour of the Mong Tok markets and shopping areas (wet market, ladies鈥?market, flower market, electronics.) Don鈥檛 miss it. It鈥檚 a bargain. Mong Tok is VERY crowded 鈥?always. So, keep the map provided by the hotel handy.Apart from shopping in the Mong Tok area, during the two days we stayed in HK, we took the Star Ferry鈥檚 (Victoria) Harbour tour (Hopping Pass). Check out the Clock Tower at the terminal. If you are lucky, you will see some junks on the harbour. Also cross the harbour from Kowloon and take the tram up from Central MTR station on Hong Kong Island up to Victoria peak for a great view of the harbour. Travelling round HK is easy. Despite the warnings about taxis, we had no problems: they are cheap, efficient, and in abundance. But the MTR is really the way to go. Also cheap, clean, efficient - and faster than taxi. If you need change for the ticket machines, the customer services staff provides it. Take the MTR to Tung Chung on Lantau Island, near the airport, where you can take the memorable cable car ride up to the Giant Buddha, Po Lin Monastery and Chinese鈥搒tyle village at Ngong Ping (one of the best attractions in HK).

<Content>Loved Langham Place Having arrived on an early morning flight from Sydney, we were delighted to find our room available.We had booked the hotel after reading the reviews on TripAdvisor, and were not disappointed. Whilst the hotel is out of the main area for tourist hotels, there is very much the feeling of being in the middle of real Hong Kong life. Street markets are just around the corner. I would love to return to this hotel again.

<Author>TommyTV
<Content>Incredible attention to detail I think this hotel will probably be the standard we use for all hotels we stay at in the future. It was our 40th Wedding anniversary and so I had decided on a cruise, with 5 days at the Langham Place to start with. We booked their limousine service from the airport, and we were met by a hotel representative who gave us maps and bottled water while we waited a couple of minutes for the Limo to arrive. Baggage loaded, we were driven directly to the ground floor entrance where we were met by a group of bell-hops to take care of our luggage, whilst an assistant then took us up to the 36th floor to Club L, got us a glass of champagne each and sorted out our room cards. As all drinks and food are free in Club L. we stayed a couple of hours talking with other guests before retiring at 1 a.m. to our suite on the 37th floor, which I have to say was much larger than I had imagined possible in Hong Kong. Waiting for us was a free bottle of chmpagne on ice, a presentation platter of cocolate coated strawberries, and a plate of chocolate leaves on sugar. It was the first time we have had a suite with two restrooms (toilets for Brits). There was a lounge area with a 42 gas plasma and the usual hotel entertainment channels, a bar area with fridge and coffee/tea making facilities, a single toilet, then a seperate bedroom with a kingsize bed and even a menu for pillows. Attached to the bedroom is a glass bathroom (with motorised blinds for privacy) and more than adequate wardrobes. Again there was a 37 plasma on the wall. By the side of the bed was a clock/radio with an I-Pod docking station and a remote for the I-pod. The telphone system in the room allows you to take a small handset with you around the hotel.Although a continental breakfast was available in Club L, we opted for the breakfast in The Place, which had a fantastic selection, similar to that on a cruise ship - something for most nationalities including bacon, eggs, sausages, beans, mushrooms and hash browns with toast.They say the devil is in the detail, and on the day of our 40th, we dined in the Ming Court. The staff are so attentive that they must have noticed my wife is left-handed, and moved her chopsticks and glass over to her left hand. Only a small thing, but very impressed that they noticed. We used the pool on the roof (accesible through the Spa) which was really nice, however they could do with waiter service on sunny days, although towels and comfortable sunbeds were available. The concierge was excellent, we asked him to recommend a good steak restaraunt. and he sent us to Mortens of Chicago in the Sheraton Hotel next to The Peninsula on the waterfront. Again fantastic service and great ambience. The bill was astronomic - $HK2700 for wine and two main courses ($US370, 拢180) but the taxi back was incredibly cheap ($US3.00, 拢1.50) for a 15 minute journey. Travelling around is very cheap - get an Octopus card for $HK150 which includes $HK50 deposit, use it all week, and then take it back and they refund the unused part and the deposit. The Langham Place is in a great area for walking around - Mong Kok feels and looks properly Chinese unlike Hong Kong island which felt like the financial district of a capital city, not much local atmosphere. We also felt very safe.Shopping was really no cheaper than the UK, but if you need tailored clothing, visit Eddie Siu on Hanoi Road, T.S.T Kowloon. Proper Chinese tailor and everything I bought is perfect. I bought a made-to-measure jacket from an Asian tailor which although very cheap ($150, 拢75) is nowhere near the same quality.Checkout at the Langham Place was a breeze as they sort everytthing out in Club L. We stayed another day on our return from the cruise in a normal room which although smaller was still a reasonable size and well appointed.I would recommend this hotel without reserve. From umbrellas to bathrobes, they think of everything .Martin Tetlow

<Content>OK Hotel I stayed at Langham Place from 27 - 29 March 2008. <Author>Shopaholiday
<Content>Phenomenally good experience Cannot praise the Langham Place highly enough. Hotel staff extremely polite, welcoming and efficient. I'd booked a car to collect me at the airport - the hotel has a desk in arrivals, and there I was met with smiles and presented with a soft drink and a Sony PSP playing an informative video about the hotel, which I watched in a very nice Mercedes during the half-hour transfer to the city. We upgraded our room on arrival to a Club room - this was located on the 35th floor with views out over Kowloon and the harbour. The upgrade also gave us access to the Club L lounge on the 36th floor, which more than offset any extra costs associated with the upgrade as it served light breakfasts and snacks throughout the day, as well as complimentary drinks, tea and coffee. Club L also has free internet access and its own concierge/receptionist. Room was lovely - a tad smaller than I'd expected but with top-quality features. Bathroom lovely with a big shower and a deep bath which was very welcome after long days spent sightseeing. Nice toiletries, and stuff like combs, shaving kits, toothbrushes etc available. Room had an iron and ironing board as well as a little laundry basket. Didn't need to get any laundry done so can't comment on the prices. Bed was extremely comfortable and great selection of pillows available, including hypoallergenic. An iPod dock with speakers was provided, as was a DVD player. Flat screen TV was impressive and channel choice very good, but took some time to respond to remote control! Phone system very swanky but watch out for very high costs when calling internationally. We felt safe in Mongkok although there are a few back streets that might be a little dodgy after dark if female and walking alone. Hotel is beside a huge shopping centre which has a supermarket in the basement and a 7-11 on the ground floor. It's also very close to some of the night markets - the hotel operates a free guided tour every evening at 6pm which lets you get your bearings as regards local shopping. Would recommend the Temple Street night market which is a little way from the hotel but well worth seeing. For electronics go to any branch of Fortress - they are excellent.Getting to/around Hong Kong from the hotel was simple - there's an MTR (metro) station in the basement of the adjacent shopping centre and HK Central is just a few stops south. Buy an Octopus transport card in any MTR station for 150 dollars (about 14 euro) and it'll last you several days/trips and can be topped up with cash. Tip - there's another Langham hotel in Kowloon so do make sure to bring the hotel address with you in both English and Chinese if you're planning on taking taxis as sometimes the drivers get them mixed up. I had need of a dentist on the third day of my stay and the assistant manager personally lined up an appointment for me - this was scheduled for just 90 mins after my having phoned reception for help. (Dentist in question was excellent and very reasonably priced). Finally, hotel spa was absolutely wonderful. It's on the top two floors of the hotel and there's a lovely outdoor heated pool with a small bar, as well as a very well-appointed gym. I booked a flight recovery massage for the night I arrived and it was great; also had a facial done later in the week. All in all, super service and a very relaxing stay at the Langham Place. Would definitely stay there again.  
<Date>Mar 31, 2008

<Author>CSRC
<Content>Faultless Stayed in a Club L room for 5 nights, and I can't think of a single complaint. The room was smallish but well thought out, so it didn't feel cramped at all. The bed was probably the most comfortable I've slept in. The huge flatscreen TV could be watched from the bath, thanks to the glass wall on the bathroom. The club was great - the best in any hotel I've stayed in. Drinks served all day, with sparkling wine until 6pm and then Mumm until 1am. There was a lavish afternoon tea and good canapes in the evening, followed by a dessert buffet. There were plenty of computers and two great massage chairs. Continental breakfast was served in the lounge, or you could choose the very comprehensive breakfast service in the main restaurant (incl dim sum, miso soup, sushi, congee on top of the usual staples).The staff were great - we didn't have one unpleasant experience. Contrary to some reports, I found the staff to be more genuine and friendly than in many large hotels. In addition, the turn down service was so comprehensive they cleaned the bathroom! This is a bit environmentally indulgent, but it is very luxurious to have a clean bathroom and dry towels for both your evening and morning showers. The pool facilities are very nice, with steam room, sauna and oriental hot tub in the change rooms, as well as a jacuzzi next to the pool. The gym was really good, with plenty of equipment, personal tvs on the machines and great views.We found the location to be ideal - Mong Kok is definitely a less touristy area that Tsim Sha Tsui or Central, which for us was a bonus. The MRT is in the same building as the hotel, but it is actually quite an interesting walk down to Tsim Sha Tsui from the hotel. We enjoyed walking to the Temple St night markets for excellent seafood, and from there it is another short walk to the many outdoor bars of Knutsford Terrace. The mall below the hotel is a shopping destination in its own right. Will definitely stay at the Langham Place again - it was a faultless experience.

<Author>CPS200
<Content>Good Hotel but not a 5 star I had a fine stay at the Langham Place Hotel but I was slightly disappointed with the size of the hotel room on arrival. It was a standard room and it was very small. I was able to upgrade to a studio suite (for extra cost) which was much more similar to a 5 star hotel room. The staff was warm and helpful. The restaurants in the hotel were very good-the price of the buffet breakfast was expensive.( We opted to get in a cab and have breakfast at the Intercontiental Hotel that overlooks the water and city for roughly the same price). I am not sure I would stay here again-the location is not great for a tourist. I spent a lot of time on the metro or in a cab. I think I would have better off in Central. The rooms are cheaper due to the location versus other 5 star hotels but ,frankly, this is not a 5 star hotel. Other 4 star hotels are the same price in but have better locations.

<Author>Sagodo
<Content>Great hotel, shame about check-in We have just returned from a week's stay at Langham Place in Mongkok. We had a lovely time apart from a bad experience at check-in.We took the limo transfer from the airport to the hotel where we were offered soft drinks and newspapers and were given a PSP with a video presentation about the hotel. The staff at the airport and the driver were helpful and friendly.Once at the hotel, the check-in was quick and easy, but we did not find the staff particularly welcoming or pleasant. On leaving the lift at our floor, we noticed a strong smell of smoke and on entering our room we found it also to smell and have an ash-tray and matches. We booked our room well in advance, at the time requesting a non-smoking room and reconfirmed this the day before we travelled. We were not told at check-in that no non-smoking rooms were available and were allocated a smoking room. We called the S.M.A.R.T Centre (guest helpline) and were told that no other rooms were available and they would send cleaners to carry out an air treatment within the next ten minutes. After waiting for 45 minutes with no sign of the cleaners, we went directly to reception to try and get the matter sorted. They were suprised that the cleaners had not arrived and offered to send the cleaners back immediately. We didn't think this was acceptable after waiting so long, and asked to be moved to another room. After another 10 minutes of two members of staff looking at the computer and talking to each other in Chinese, a non-smoking room suddenly became available. Although this room was on a lower level, we had no choice but to accept it as we were tired after 13 hours of travelling and just wanted to get to our room. No real apology was made apart from a sorry for the inconvenience as we left to go to the new room. It was not the level of service we would expect from this standard of hotel.Our room was lovely as other reviewers have described. We booked an Executive room which we found to be of a good size with lots of storage space, which was handy as we were staying a week. The bed was very big and extremely comfy with lots of extra of pillows. The bathroom had an amazing walk-in shower and separate bath with plenty of amenities, e.g. toothbrush, razor, cottonwool, comb etc. The glass wall was an excellent idea to see the view or TV from your bath, but also had a blind if you wanted privacy. Cleanliness was of a very high standard.We had breakfast at the hotel every day. The restaurant was a lovely setting with a huge choice of western and asian food. We particularly liked the chefs who were very friendly and jolly. Breakfast closes promptly at 10.30 which the waiting staff remind you at 10.15 by pointing at their watch and bringing olive oil to the table ready for lunch!The location of the hotel was excellent and unlike other reviews, we did not find the area scary at all. We liked that we were surrounded by locals and it wasn't too touristy. The MTR station was just outside the hotel, also accessible through the adjoining mall. The mall was very modern with a huge of range of shops and restaurants and a mini supermarket in the basement.Overall, the hotel itself and its location were faultless. The staff, particuarly the chefs, concierge, housekeeping, doormen and pink ladies were extremely friendly and helpful, but were let down by the indifferent check-in staff.  
<Date>Mar 2, 2008

<Author>oneoffive
<Content>Luxury, courtesy and the best hotel I've ever visited. My friend and I stayed here for 11 nights in a twin room. It was small but beautifully furnished and the staff could not have been more helpful and efficient. From the moment we walked into the Reception area we were treated like honoured guests, nothing was too much trouble for the staff. From the lift ladies to the pool attendants, they were a delight. Halfway through our trip, on a public holiday, my friend became ill and needed the attention of a doctor and an injection. The hotel arranged all this for us and we had an english-speaking doctor at our room within 2 hours. The facilities at the hotel were wonderful, the roof-top pool was perfect after a long day's shopping and the restaurant breakfasts were fantastic. The location of the hotel was great too. We had been to Hong Kong before and knew that the MTR (like the Tube or the Metro) was clean, easy to navigate and wonderfully convenient - the station for the MTR is at the bottom of the shopping mall which ajoins the hotel. So you can get off the plane, on to the train and go to your hotel within an hour. The mall was open late (shops in HK often don't open until around 10am but stay open till about 11pm) and the food courts there were fantastic. The concierge was also very helpful with hints on good restaurants to visit and information about opening hours and travel choices.We saved up for our trip for years and we did worry that our expectations would be too high for any holiday to live up to. The Langham hotel exceeded all of them, from the DVD player and the complimentary water, to the delicious room service burgers when we got hungry in the middle of the night, to the doormen who translated for us with the taxi drivers. I plan to return to HK in a couple of years, I'll be staying here again. (In fact, I've stayed at another Langham - Auckland - since and it is just as delightful.)

<Author>shazza_h
<Content>Loved the Langham It is not surprising that The Langham Place in Hong Kong is ranked at number 1. We spent 5 days at the LP during our honeymoon. We booked the hotel limo service to and from the airport via dealing directly with the hotel. All communication with the hotel was fast, efficient and professional. Finding the hotel desks at the airport is a bit of a challenge. As a tip, walk straight through the arrivals hall and all the hotel desks are situated on the very far right hand corner, right at the back. We spent a good while finding it! The cost of the hotel limi is 550 HKD each way (around 33 GBP). We checked in on the club level and were given a beautiful suite on the 36th floor. We took advantage of the 'Suite Dreams' package and I think its definately good value for money. The Club Level is certainly worth the extra cost. It's lovely to have somewhere to go when you are jet lagged and need a snack at 3am! Non alcoholic drinks are provided 24/7 and alcoholic drinks during most of the day - a few hours in the early morning when they are not provided.The rooms are absolutely beautiful. Our suite was complete with 2 bathrooms, 2 big plasma screens, a massive bed and 5 telephones throughout! The rooms were made up in the morning and then given a quick once over in the evening (fresh towels and turn down service). We had a view over the city and can look down into the bustling streets below. Breakfast was included with the deal. You can either have continental breakfast at the Club Level or in the main restaurant 'The Place'. We only ate at The Place and the selection and service was exceptional. There is a good mix between Chinese fare and more traditional breakfast items (fresh omlettes, bacon, hash browns, fruit, toast etc).Also included as part of the package was a spa treatment. My husband and I both had wonderful hour long massage treatments at their beautiful spa on the 41st floor. The gym at the hotel was also amazing. Definately the best gym I've ever seen at a hotel. All the equipment was modern, clean and the cardio equipment was near the window overlooking the city.One of the best assets to the hotel are the staff. The hotel is very professionally run and is apparent that their staff are trained very well. One other reviewer commented on the youthfullness of the staff. This is certainly something we noted as well.Agreed, the location is somewhat out of the way, but it does provide an element of authenticity being in a heavily populated local area. We did not take the underground to get around, instead we did a local tour which we booked via the hotel concerige. It was the half day Hong Kong Island Orientation tour. The cost was 320 HKD each. I think this is well worth it as it takes you to Victoria Peak and Stanley Market as some of the highlights. We found Stanley Market somewhat disappointing compared the ladies market which is just 2 blocks from the hotel. But then again, we were visiting during Chinese New Year and some of the shops were closed.The hotel is also connected to a large shopping mall. This is great for quick and inexpensive meal options.Overall, 10 out of 10 for the Langham Place. We will definately be back next time we are in Hong Kong.

Every part of the hotel gleamed. For Hong Kong we think think we got good value for our money. We highly recommend the Club rooms at this wonderful hotel for a first class experience.

<Author>Herbert Hallman
<Content>Decent value for the money in pricey H.K. While I'm less euphoric than some or other recent reviwers this is undeniably a well functioning hotel. I do have a slight problem with the location. While by no means remote, it is a good cab or subway ride to the scene of most of the action, the reason we come to H.K. Yes, the Mong Kok station is quite close, but one still has to buy a ticket, get to the platform and often stand in the jam packed cars. Mind you, the fare is cheap and the cars modern and clean, but it's still a subway. The service at this ultra modern hotel is excellent: fast, efficient and invariably friendly. The club lounge is one of the best I've ever encountered and well worth the additional cost. I must confess that I like the idea of getting a chilled beer--or any other beverage for that matter (with alcohol or sans) at, say, 1 p.m rather than wait for the freebies at 5:30 or 6 p.m. A generous and wise policy on the part of hotel management. We occupied an executive suite on the 39th floor which, while not huge, was well configured and even had a small kitchen (kitchenette). The view was nothing special, but that partly relected the room location and lousy weather (heavy overcast). One minor complaint was the over airconditioned lobby and restaurant where breakfast is served ( the first two mornings we foolishly skipped the lounge, thinking it would not be as elaborate. Big mistake: it was even better than downstairs and the classy, intimate atmosphere made the occasion much more relaxing, not to mention it wasn't freezing). Would I return? Very possibly, but after 7 visits to H.K. (my first in Oct. '56) I've grown a bit tired of the place. It's become very pricey and--maybe I'm showing my age--too frenetic as well. Moreover the shopping is either too high-end or real kitchy (Mong Kok). Lastly, the air quality, never its long suit, has really deteriorated. Yet if you've never been there (is there anyone who hasn't?), it remains--not unlike Vegas--a must. But for my money, if given the choice, Victoria Island or harborside Kowloon would be a better locale, especially for the first time visitor. Herb Hallman  Denver, CO

<Author>Scothol
<Content>Great hotel - except for location We chose the Langham Place because of the reviews on Tripadvisor and we were delighted with it. Our only negative comment would be the location - it is in a rundown area and the checkout questionnaire of the hotel actually asks guests whether they 'felt safe' walking out of the hotel. The answer is that we did not, especially as tourists are warned to be wary of pickpockets.In the event, we had no problems but the next time, I think we would try the sister hotel, the Langham, which is much nearer the ferry terminal and other attractions. Incidentally, we were surprised how little English some taxi drivers could understand. We only discovered on our second day that the hotel can provide a small booklet listing numerous likely destinations, including the hotel itself, in Chinese script. This was very helpful.

<Author>DeveA666
<Content>As city hotels go........ Slap bang in the middle of Mong Kok, 25 mins from the airport is this impressive structure connected to a shopping mall which is at best average by HK's high shopping standards.Check in on a Thursday evening was rapid we chose this hotel on kowloon side as we were there for business. This hotel was The Business.StaffImmediate upgrade to larger triple with excellent views. Reception staff were first class, concierge service was equally as gracious with an ambundance of local knowledge from advice as to where to get a good pint to the best place for toys, complete with a beware the quality reminder. I did require a doctor whilst there as I had forgot to pack some cruical medication that was available on prescription only. The duty manager spoke to me in person and advised me to go to my room whilst he sorted this out within 5 minutes I was on the phone to the hotels sub contracted doctor who advised me to travel to see him as it would be quicker and cheaper. From pressing the lift buttons for you to helping you in and out of taxi's, to there genuine pleasure in serving you. This was a refreshing change and something staff at the supposed super resorts in Dubai (I have Madinat Jumeirah in Mind) should take note of. Truly truly gob smacking pioneering customer service with little touches everywhere, amazing gracious service.The room, all mod cons, plasma, dvd, stereo, wireless keyboard for the internet (chargeable), quiet and reliable air con, nice window seat built into the ledge, reasonable min bar prices, pillow menu, slippers, gown etc. The rooms are fresh, crisp, well maintained, bathrooms are spacious enough and the 'open' bathroom is easily rectified by simply drawing the blinds.Restaurants and bars Very good from bar snacks, to the chinese (Ming Court I think?) restaurant the food quality is good. You do have an awful amount of choice within the attached shopping centre from mcdonalds, deli france, pizzas so if you are budgeting and saving cash for the shops its pitched well for you.LocationDon't be put off by Mong Kok. Its not rough by Uk standards its quite charming and has a chinese bustle to it. You are safe and there are more than enough shops in the immediate locality for you to have a browse around. There is a shortage of good local bars however but don't worry. Its only 60-80 HKD to the Wan Chai bars and central. Again same price to the Mall at Harbour city which is a good one in my opinion. You can also use the MTR which is 4 mins from the hotel. Clean, fast and efficient a pleasure to use, journey time into central/ causeway bay 10 mins max. You can also use the star ferry(pennies) on the Kowloon side which will drop you island side adjacent to harbour city mall which is a good spot to take the classic harbour panoramic photo. I have no qualms about staying Kowloon side the hotels tend to be cheaper.OverallI've been a very lazy trip advisor for years. I should have posted reviews about the Atlantis Bahamas, Loewes Miami beach, Mina A Salam Dubai, Westin Times Square New York, numerous eastern shangri la's. This hotel beats the pants off them and I will be using them again in April/mayThis Hotel its not a beach resort if it was the sand would be raked hourly men would clean your sunglasses every 15 minutes, fruit cocktails on sticks, cucumbers for the eyes etc. The hotel and its staff are excellent go and enjoy a fantastic city hotel.Flights Virgin (Direct booking) Truly Rubbish service both ways and I like Virgin.Hotel Booked via expedia excellent rate, though Asiarooms.com had excellent rates for April 2008 when I last checked.

<Author>fred_shen
<Content>Great hotel Stayed Jan 2-7, 2008. At first a little apprehensive - website looks great, but a little out of the way in Mongkok. But when you arrive, the room was great. Thoroughly modern, great views (we were on the 31st floor). The bed and pillows were the best I have slept in. I asked the hotel where to buy the pillows. Only drawback was the extra charge for in-room internet. However, the 5th floor had a number of internet terminals and most of the time we did not have to wait to use. Service staff were very polite and helpful.Was confused how to get from airport to hotel so emailed the hotel - response was fantastic with detailed maps depending on your choice of transportation. We chose the express bus. On leaving the hotel, we took a cab to the Kowloon station to grab the airport train (fast and cheap). Told them our choice and they registered our names with the bus desk. Easy.The hotel connected to a mall which was convenient as we ate breakfast there and had Starbucks there. The mall had many restaurants, including a pretty good dim sum (recommended). The dessert place was very good as well (also recommended).The location of the hotel, while initially I had misgivings, is not too bad. Close to the Mongkok MTR so convenient. Also close to the Mongkok East station which we took the MTR to Shenzhen for a day of shopping. Around the hotel are many shopping places. The street for shoes is close by as is the night market stalls. Also, many snack places if you like street food.

<Author>ATLCTC
<Content>The Reviews Are true!! I chose this hotel based on the reviews from the TripAdvisor.com website. I was not disappointed.Just to be clear, this hotel is not located on Hong Kong Island (the postcard views of the big buildings). It is on the Kowloon side in a neighborhood called Mong Kok. The hotel could not be more convenient though. It is attached to a very modern mall (Langham Place Mall) and you can access the subway (MTR) from this Mall. The MTR will take you into Hong Kong Island (Admiralty stop or Central stop) for HK$ 10.50. The cost of transportation in Hong Kong is very reasonable (e.g. subways and taxis).The hotel is very well appointed and the staff could not be nicer. I was there for 6 days and the level of service stayed very high the entire stay.Make sure you check out the gym/spa on the 41st floor. The view from the Relaxation Corner is great. You can see the skyline of Kowloon and Hong Kong Island as well as the harbour. Every night at 8:00pm, the buildings on Hong Kong Island put on a light show. It is one of the world's great skyline views.There is a Starbucks and a McDonalds located in the Langham Place mall if you can't seem to leave the US behind. There are also some cool street markets in the neighborhoods around the hotel. You may never eat Chinese food again after visiting these markets, but they are definitely part of the Hong Kong experience.Make sure you take a trip to the South side of Hong Kong Island (Repulse Bay and Stanley). On a clear, sunny day, Stanley seems like Italy or Greece to me.Have a good time and stay at the Langham Place Hotel. You will not be disappointed.  
<Date>Jan 16, 2008

<Author>GaylePDublin
<Content>Great hotel Stayed here for two nights in October and have to agree with most of what has already been written. The hotel is excellent, part of a big shopping mall and also right beside the buzzing and fascinating Mongkok. If you want to be down near Hong Kong itself with views of the bay then this is not the place to stay but we went down that part of the city several times quite easily by MTR or taxi and did not feel we were missing out by staying in Mongkok. In fact it was quite refreshing to be staying somewhere a little different. We were in a standard room but found it well above average, though small. The glass walled bathroom was quirky and the bathroom itself well stocked. Bed was comfortable. The only small criticisms were that there was some very obvious damp in the bathroom and the internet in the room was very expensive. Staff overall were friendly and efficient and we used the concierge service for restaurant recommendations and other information. Finally a word has to go to the fabulous rooftop pool and the magnificent spa. Prices for the treatments might seem a little off putting but are well worth it. We stayed here as part of a three month trip around the world and this was the best spa we came across.

<Author>LightEntertainment
<Content>Great rooms, great amenities and great location The Langham Place Hotel in Mongkok is a very stylish, very modern and very comfortable hotel. Its location is great; only a few minutes work to the Mongkok MTR station and only a quick 15min cab ride to central. The Langham Place is surrounded by great shops; it even has its own 13 story shopping mall across the street connected by a walkway.We booked a Club Level room online, and when we arrived we were escorted to a private check-in. Believe me, the Club rooms are well worth the extra price because they come with a huge range on complimentary services: free wired/wireless internet, free use of the gym/swimming pool, access to a private lounge on Level 36 and free breakfast.The hotel as a whole is great, as mentioned before. The dining options available are top notch, with a range of Western and Cantonese food available; the rooms are great; the roof top swimming pool and gym is first class and what is more, the staff are extremely friendly and helpful.I recommend this hotel to anyone not scared off by the high prices, mind you we did stay there over New Years, so I presume it would be a fair bit cheaper at less popular times. The Club rooms are well worth the extra price. And the stay was just great all round.

<Author>FussyGlobeTrotter
<Content>Good value for money for HK I lived in Langham Place for 4 months in 2007 and have stayed there a total of 10 or so times in the past few years.The basic rooms are small and the finish on many rooms is a little cheap for a 5 star (veneer panelling, poor grouting technique in the bathrooms, cheap knobs and buttons etc), but the rooms are generally well appointed, modern, feel clean and new and are good value for money for what you get in Hong Kong. (I lived here remember, so I experienced many, many, many rooms so maybe I am being a little fussy, but hey.... I kept coming back).I would recommend upgrading to the executive room as the bathrooms are that little bit nicer with glass walls and separate shower.The hotel pool is small but nice, and the change rooms (AKA, relaxing havens) are wonderful. I used them all the time as they felt like a day spa. They had piped relaxing music, stone finishes, candles, plunge pool, sauna, steam room, mirror backed showers, lockers, facilities for getting ready like hairdryers, cotton buds, mini towels. They even have a machine that sucks the water from your swimsuit! The staff are great and we have always had a great time here. The 'pink ladies' manning the lifts are useless, but a nice touch! lol.I always get my family and friends to consider staying here when they visit Hong Kong because the suburb of Mong Kok is a great base for tourists. At the Lanham Place, you step out of your luxe hotel into the one of the most densely populated parts of Hong Kong and are in the thick of things. It is right near the Mong Kok MTR and hundreds of buses to almost every part of Hong Kong run up and down Nathan Rd which is close by.The Langham Place Mall (shopping) is connected to the hotel and has some OK restaurants and kitsch Asian shopping experiences. Also, if you wanted to walk through this mall to the MTR and travel to many other shopping malls underground by train all across HK, you could in fact never have to go outside if it's bucketing with rain or hot. At the end of the day, the hotel bar is great and they always have jazz singers to entertain. It's a great spot to meet before heading out.All of the Qantas staff stay here too, so it's interesting to watch the pilots and stewards arriving and departing for each flight to and from Melbourne/Sydney. At least you always know when you'd better leave for the airport to catch your flight back home!

<Author>jimmac_7
<Content>If you're going to HK stay here! We stayed at the Langham Place for 3 nights at the end of a 2 week honeymoon in thailand and what a fantastic place. It has everything - great service, great style, great rooms and one of the best hotel swimming pools anywhere in the world. The first thing I would say is don;t be put off by the Location. The hotel is attached to the Langham Place Mall which is enormous with some 300 shops and some great restaurants. The Mong Kok MTR station is about 20m away and is only 2 stops from Tsim Tsha Sui. It also goes to Central on HK island. Mong Kok itself is bustling with real HK life. We liked it becuase it away from the Tsim Tsha Sui tourist trap where you get hasled every 10m by hawkers.We opted for the Limo service from the airport which is a great way to see some of HK. If you get talking to your driver he will give you a guided tour on the trip. On arriving at the hotel we were met by the concierge which consists of an extremely polite young lady dressed in a red suit with a red hat. These concierge seem to be a trademark of the hotel as they appear everywhere and have no other purpose than to say good morning/afternoon/night and calling lifts for you. The recpetionist was Japanese and spoke perfect english. She was very efficient and made us feel very welcome. Without even asking we were given a late check out on our last day as our flight back to the UK wasn't until late in the evening. Whilst waiting to check in the hot face towels we were provided with was a nice touch.The rooms are very smart indeed, although not the biggest. Most of the space is taken up by the very comfortable king size bed. The duvet and pillows are of the highest quality. The bathroom is also quite special. The sink unit is one big piece of moulded glass which means you can see all the stylish chrome pipe work. The whole room is filled with mirrors to make what is a small bathroom seem much larger. The partition wall between the bathroom and bedroom is glass with a pull down screen. This means you can see the TV from the bath. The shower is the best I've ever had. There are some great gadgets in the bedroom itself. The air con is touch screen, the flat screen TV has an excellent virtual concierge that explains how everything in the room works. The telephone is also very useful. Its a Cisco IP Telephony phone which basically means that you can search the internet with it. It will provide you with things like the weather, news, exchange rate etc. It also lets you book a table in the restaurants and spa treatments. You can also get tube and city maps at the touch of a button - very useful.If you get chance and are that way inclined take a visit to the gym. The views are incredible and the position of the running machines are enough to make anyone want to take up running. The swimming pool is also fantastic. Its open air but the pool is so warm. Its on the top floor (42nd) and needless to say the views are pretty impressive.All in all this is an extremely impressive hotel. The service is very slick and everything is done with a touch of style. I would definitely reccommend this to anyone visiting HK and if I back that way in the future I will definitely stay here again.  
<Date>Dec 24, 2007

<Author>Travelingmaven
<Content>The Other Reviews Said It All! I rely almost totally on TripAdvisor reviews when booking hotels, so was expecting a marvelous experience at the Langham Place Hotel. I was not disappointed! I have been to Hong Kong 4 times, but this time I decided to take my children  their spouses (party of 6) for 5 nights. I figured Mong Kok would be more fun for them than elsewhere,  wanted a somewhat newish hotel for their introduction to one of the world's most exciting cities. The Langham Place Hotel was perfect! Check-in was easy, probably because we had e-mailed our requests ahead of time. There was a large convention of cardiologists in the hotel plus a wedding when we arrived, yet it didn't seem crowded. The rooms we had were on different floors with varied views, but all wonderful. I note that the hotel offers Sunday entertainments for children, which was quite a nice touch. There are changing signs in the lobby (on the 4th floor) that detail coming events. I particularly liked the fact that the bar had rolling BBC headlines, and that at breakfast the placemats showed newsheadlines, DJIA, and stock market closes from around the world. Breakfast was great! Dim sum, sushi, eggs made to request, hot and cold cereals, fresh honey comb, fresh fruits (even lichees!), and some of the best, flaky pastries I've ever had. Breakfast was included in our hotel room price, BTW. The Ming Court restaurant has superb food, altho the English translations of the dishes leaves a bit to be desired (I had difficulty thinking about eating fungus for example, altho I know they meant mushroom). The decor is sleek, accented with excellent quality reproductions of bronzes and ceramics found in the Mong Kok area. Prices are not inexpensive  everything is a la carte ($5 US for a Tsing Tsao beer; $10 US for a glass of wine; $10 for a salad; $30 entree), but the quality is worth it. We wanted to return to Loong Yuen, a fabulous restaurant in the basement of the Holiday Inn (yes, really!), so asked the concierge to make a reservation for us. He did, but with the caveat that we would have to be finished by 8:30 because the restaurant had been booked for a wedding. When we arrived, we were surprised to find that the chef had put together a special menu just for us, complete with a Private Reserve Shiraz wine. How nice for the Concierge to request that special treat on his own!The rooms are adequate in size - actually quite large by HK standards. There is a desk, with desk chair, TV, Smart Phone, chest of drawers, 2 bedside tables, an arm chair, small refrig, accoutrments for fixing coffee or tea, a nice-sized closet with ironing board  iron. Again, there are charges for beverages and coffee/tea. However, we received 2 bottles of complimentary water daily. The toiletries provided were fine - nothing special, but I really liked the turn-down service with slippers. We didn't have kimonos in our room, like my children did, but the terry-cloth bathrobes were nice. The spa treatments were impressive (price reduction if booked between 8-10 a.m.). For $200 US you get a 2 hour pampering: facial, mud wrap, accupressure massage. What could be better after a day running around Hong Kong  Kowloon?Check out went smoothly. There were no surprises on the bill. Our bags were picked up promptly. All in all, I'd rate this hotel highly, and would return in a heartbeat. The food and staff are stupendous!

<Author>jwl2672
<Content>Great with one exception (phone calls) I booked this hotel for my parents' 2-week vacation to Hong Kong. They haven't been back for 40 years so I thought that it'd be nice to stay in a 5-star hotel. They told me the stay was excellent and that the free breakfast (must book a package to receive) was spectacular - it included all sorts of culinary delights from dim sum to sushi to omelettes cooked to order, etc.The one problem was that upon checking out, they discovered that their phone calls were $25HKD each. These were calling card calls to New York City (thus, a local number). What's more, the package we booked stated specifically free local calls.  They complained but the receptionist claimed that all hotels charge if you dial using a calling card. That's absurd. They made 30 such calls which becomes a hefty sum. They really need to state explicitly that long distance calls using calling cards are charged.Other than that, everything else was great. We asked them if we could take 2 tours instead of the included 1 free tour and it was approved.

<Content>This Hotel is Certainly A Number 1! Stayed there for 5 nights. This hotel is the best I have come across in all my travels. The rooms were very comfortably but what is more important, the hotel has thought of everything that a traveller would need to feel at home and well-looked after. The room has a Cisco Smart Phone and all one needs to do to ask for service or help is just to press one button. The SMART operator functions like a one-stop service personal for everything - from laundry, to food, to setting you up for a quick checking out etc. SPA is just excellent and the gym is 24 hours. I have stayed in many hotel and I always have issues with the opening hours of the gym. They normally start at 6.30 am and there isn't enough time to get in an hour of exercise and then be heading out for a meeting at 8.30 am unless I skip breakfast. The concierge provided boxes, sticky tap and strings for packing - something a traveller who is doing some heavy shopping would need. The room was also very well thought out. The whole place smells clean and good. The hotel is just next to Langham Place a shopping centre with lost of retail space and food! It sits on top of the Mongkok station and I think one can't ask for more in terms of location. Food around the area is readily available and Electronic, Sports and Ladies Market just a short walk away.

<Author>EmmaBea
<Content>Amazing! Couldn't fault it! Stay here Having read previous reviews of this hotel on TripAdvisor I had high expectations - which I can safely say were met and exceeded! Everyone going to Hong Kong should stay here!Hotel Location: 5 mins walk to the MTR (tube) station. 5 mins walk from ladies market and sports market, 10 mins walk to goldfish market and flower market. Roughly 15mins MTR ride to Star ferry and Kowloon area.Hotel rooms: very luxury, clean, everything you could possibly need and more! We paid the extra for a Club room and it was worth it - although I am sure the other rooms in the hotel were just as nice. Rooms have massive flat screen tv, wireless access, ipod docking station (in Club rooms), rain power shower, complimentary water and chocolates/slippers by the bed at night! Floor to ceiling windows had a lovely view of the city. Room also had a free of charge safe for guest use.Club L facilities: free of charge drinks (alcohol included) all day/night plus snacks and continental breakfast. Internet access with computers, library, DVD library and personalised check in. I thought it was worth paying the extra for the free drinks and snacks, plus the internet access was handy.Hotel food: Room service was excellent value and prompt. We also paid for the full breakfast (Club breakfast was continental only) and this was an amazing selection (e.g. english,omlettes, pancakes) and very tasty. If you are happy with continental only then don't bother paying the extra for this! We went to the chinese restaurant in the hotel which was of a very high standard. We also ate in The Place which serves a buffet style menu in the evenings which was again delicious.Other hotel facilities: Hotel roof top swimming pool and jacuzzi was absolutely lovely and just what you needed after a day of sightseeing! Chaun Spa was most relaxing too - I recommend! The shopping centre next to the hotel was great and very big, so take some time to go around it all!! Its great to just walk back over the bridge to the hotel to drop your purchases off!!Other tips for HK overall: 1.Buy an Octopus card, you can use this for all bus/train/MTR travel including the Peak Tram  bus to Po Lin Monastery.2. Go on the free Mongkok markets tour the hotel offers - a lovely lady took us round and gave some great tips. One of which is to visit the sports market near the hotel - lots of trainers, both for casual and sports wear - at good prices.3. Go to Stanley market on the other side of Hong Kong island.Overall, I would definitely recommend staying here, the staff at the hotel were so kind and professional, it makes such a welcome change to have such a high standard of customer service. The staff really do predict what your needs are going to be before you even ask them!!

<Content>Langham Place - best place outside of Central Langham Place is a great hotel in Mongkok. If you're heading to Hong Kong for work or pleasure this is a fantastic place to stay, without paying the high prices you'll find in Central - and only a few train stops away. Langham Place is connected to Langham Mall....a very trendy mega-mall, almost a bit too trendy for my tasts, but interesting to see what the latest fads are. It's also a few blocks away from Ladies Market, Electronics Market, and Sports Market for some interesting night bargain shopping. The hotel iteself is fabulous - the bathroom shares a glass wall with the hotel room, very cool. My favorite part is the negative edge rooftop pool and high-end exercise room. The morning breaksfast is also fabulous, a great selection of fruits, breads, and hot foods.

<Author>Sharpie2
<Content>Just what the Dr ordered Stayed at the Langham Place for 9 nights from 8th November. I had booked the hotel following such wonderful reviews on Trip Advisor and was not disappointed. The trip was a suprise for my husband's 40th and it certainly was a trip to remember. I had booked a club level room with access to the club lounge. When we checked in - not in the lobby but in the club lounge with a cup of tea and a hot towel - they asked us if we'd like to upgrade to a suite. I was quite happy with the room I had originally booked so declined. However, they gave us the suite anyway. So, just keep this in mind. What can I say about the hotel which has not already been reported. The staff are wonderful. Concierge can tell you anything you need to know and give you the easy way to get around. They were just wonderful. We purchased an Octopus card which is the greatest creation going and travelled everywhere by MTR; Star Ferry and Bus. The transport system is one of the best I have ever come across. The location of the hotel is, in my opinion, perfect. The markets are all on your doorstep, I felt safe everytime I went out on my own to do a spot of shopping whilst my husband and son had a swim early evening. We had breakfast in The Place each morning as the variety is so vast compared to the Club lounge which is just continental. But the lounge itself is well worth the extra if you are considering. Afternoon tea from around 3pm- 5.30; Canapes from 6pm - 8pm and dessert from 8pm - 10pm. A good variety of wine; spirits; soft drinks and champagne. As first time visitors to HK, we never tired of sitting in the window with a drink in hand looking out over the skyline towards HK island and watching the light show around 8pm. The two massage chairs in the lounge are wonderful, and have loads of settings including one just for your feet and legs which was much needed after a long flight. Ellie in the Club lounge was excellent - she would arrange anything for you and could not do enough to help which must be said of all the staff. I could go on and on about how wonderful the Langham Place is - however,it would take you days to read! If you need to know anything in particular, please feel free to ask. For a treat of pure luxury in the busy lives we all lead, the Langham is just what the Doctor ordred! Enjoy!

<Author>Bannerman-7
<Content>Nice hotel We stayed at Langham Place for 3 nights over a weekend and were pleased we chose this hotel.All the staff were very friendly and were happy to assist in any way they could.The room was modern and clean with a fantastic powerfull shower, however we found the room to be on the small side as we expected a larger one for the 鈧?10 p/n incl breakfast we paid.We dined in Ming Court on our first night and had a great meal, we were surprised at how reasonable the food cost when I recieved the bill.The Shopping Mall next door has a good selection of shops, cafes and restaurants and you can go there from the hotel via an enclosed walkway.We found the best shopping to be in Causeway Bay. If you dont want to use the subway station at the hotel a Taxi from hotel will cost HK$80 incl tip one way.We did not use the hotel spa or pool but they looked great when I went to have a look around.The Bar was busy and had some good live music and there was happy hour each evening between 18:30  20:30 where drinks were 2 for 1.Free Internet with 6 Laptops was available at a location near the bar and a large Flatscreen TV to keep you up to speed on World News and Sport.The only problem we had during our stay was coming back to our room in late afternoon to find the room had not been cleaned.Each morning we left the room at 09:30 and pressed a button to request room to be cleaned so it was dissapointing to find room not cleaned on our return.I mentioned this a checkout and even filled out a form so I hope this problem will be sorted out.We had a great time at Langham Place and would stay here again when I next visit Hong Kong.

<Author>Watching_the_World
<Content>Mixed Experience Got back on Sunday and am missing their beds! The hotel is excellent at what it does and I am glad to say that overall it deserves a high ranking on TA - the basis on which I went with this hotel.Check in was a breeze, although I must add that we arrived at like 4.30am so I wouldn't really expect anything else!The rooms, we first stayed in the Deluxe rooms for 5 nights before upgrading to a couple of suites for the last two nights, were very smart and done to high quality standard. Not sure the suite's are worth the hike in the price as they dont differ enough from the usual rooms i.e. you get more floor space and a kitchen area but the furniture is pretty much the same deal and the standard rooms do it so well anyway. I suppose with a longer stay, we could have appreciated it more. One thing I will stress though, is that the beds are awesome! I am not usually so taken with hotel beds, normally they are good and you can get a good nights rest. But these were off the scale. The down pillows and duvets were just right on the mark for me to the point where I ended up asking where I could get them from!Facilities wise, the gym was nicely equipped, changing rooms incorporating a sauna, steam room and hot tub were great. As was the outdoor swimming pool on the 42nd floor.Restaurants were pretty much what you would expect from a hotel of this calibre and nothing more or less.The Club Lounge was excellent. It was organised and maintained throughout the day and during the night. The massage chairs are excellent for helping to relax after a hard day of sightseeing/shopping/conferences! The only real downside for me were some of the staff. They were not rude or impolite or anything of that nature but it seems that quite a few of them struggled with understanding my requests. If I asked for an extra coffee cup, the first response was for them to send up more coffee and sugar. Asked the concierge to help book a restaurant at Disneyland hotel, he gave me a brochure...I thought it might have been down to me but the fact is, the staff in the Lounge were absolutely excellent and I had no problems with them on similar types of requests. Not a great concern as I would be far more worred if they had attitude problems but they didnt.Location-wise, I found the hotel to be excellent. Right in the middle of a number of attractions, it was extremely well served by the MTR (on its doorstep) , its own shopping plaza and nearby parks. The only thing that put me off about the experience was the smells of Mong Kok. Its an 'interesting' mix of sewage, cooking, incense and other smells that can leave you gagging for oxygen.Luckily, this is not the case within the hotel complex but be prepared for it almost as soon as you hit the streets!That aside though, I absolutely loved the place, the hotel was fantastic overall and worth the price.If I am ever back in HK, I will be looking up Langham Place again.

<Author>DML
<Content>Great choice in Hong Kong My wife, son and I stayed at LP for three nights 9-12 November 2007 and we would hghly recommend it. After alot of research, we got the best rate through their website which included breakfast and a return limo transfer from the airport. The latter was fantastic after our long flight from LHR - even given a PSP with a video all about the hotel and HK on it. Room not the biggest (this is Hong kong) but clean with the all glass bathroom and a good view. Standard buffet breakfast - tried the evening buffet in 'The Place' one night. Good spread but quite expensive. Much better options available on several floors in the attached shopping centre. Free internet access available at computers in the work and play section. Great views from the pool, but it was a bit small and often crowded with no loungers available. We were travelling with a one year old - staff very child friendly (sometimes overpoweringly so!). Location was very good - nice walk down to Star Ferry terminal and Temple Street night market or you could easily use the MTR. Taxis actually good value as well but make sure you take the hotel-provided translation card.... not many drivers speak English! Would definitely stay here again for its relative good value, excellent location and friendly staff.

<Author>joansgirl
<Content>It's all true - Really! My ten year old daughter and I stayed at the Langham Place Hotel in Mong Kok for one night last weekend as a finale to our trip to Hong Kong. My little girl was apparently experiencing cultural overload, homesickness and travel exhaustion but the quiet luxury and friendliness of the staff soon put her at her ease. We loved the view of the harbour (including the sound and light show) from our window seat on the 30th floor. The cosiness and creature comforts of our room made it a haven from the city below. The roof-top pool was beautiful and has superb views both day and night. The spa staff were charming. We upgraded to the executive club which gave us access to nibbles and drinks when we wanted them.We really enjoyed the amazing international buffet in The Place restaurant - Indian, European, Japanese including sushi hand-made in front of you, local specialities and seafood - lots and lots of seafood - although the array of desserts was spectacular too - tiny cakes, pannacotta, creme brulee, warm English-style bread and butter pudding with vanilla cream and chocolate fountains for dipping fruit, marshmallows and waffles.The breakfast buffet was generous and catered to all tastes.The Langham Place shopping centre and Mon Kok MTR station are adjacent to the hotel and were both very busy on Saturday afternoon. There were plenty of dining choices in the mall.We used the hotel's limousine service to get us to our early homeward flight on Sunday morning. Everything went smoothly and I cannot recommend this hotel highly enough. I cannot wait to go back. Thankyou to all the staff at Langham Place, especially Fion the hostess at The Place.

<Author>IvanL
<Content>Exceptional Hotel My girlfriend and I stayed at this hotel for 5 nights in October. We booked a club room and based on what we read on tripadvisor, we had high expectations of this hotel. We were not let down...This hotel offers excellent service together with very high standards of comfort and amenities. The pool on the 42nd floor is amazing with unbelievable views over Hong Kong and Kowloon. It is situated in Mong Kok, a really busy place with markets, shops and an unbelievable amount of people. The hotel acted as a safe haven around the madness outside the doors. The room was on the 35ft floor with exceptional views. It was a large double with a fabulous shower and a very comfortable bed. As it was a club room, we availed of the bar offering drink and food all day. It is a real treat when you have been walking the streets of Hong Kong and Kowloon all day and it is definately worth the extra money when booking. The service is very personal and the staff will stand on their heads to help you. The GYM looked very well equipped but I never managed to go. The exercise you get walking the streets should be enough if you plan to take in all the sights.Food in the Hotel was OK. We ate there three times and twice had the buffet. The standard menu in the main restaurant is only OK but the buffet has all types of food catering from every pallet. If you are staying in Hong Kong, this is definately worth a look. You should not be disappointed...

<Author>DaveHampshire
<Content>Great Hotel Located in Mong Kok as soon as you step outside the Langham Place you are in the middle of the real HK - and also the most densely populated area. It's an unusual location for a 5*, but it's a weel serviced hotel with very high standards - and I mean high! If you don' tlike heights don't go here - there lifts are scenic (although a couple are enclosed) and the swimming pool on the 42nd floor treadmills face the view from the 41st.It's a good half hour walk from the harbour front, and in a busy place like this that's not easy. however MRT is just outside the Langham Place mall (connected to the hotel), and is so efficient you are anywhere in a few minutes. So all the sights are within easy reach. Concierge are very obliging, and despite other comments on the site there is no need to bribe them with big tips. Hotel breakfast is excellent (but shouldbe at the price) and the Ming Court chinese is very good indeed.Wonderful beds and pillows, and glass wall in the bathroom mean you can watch the plasma TV from the bath, and watch you other half have a --- while you lie on the bed! well, there is a blind you can pull.....Don't miss out on MongKok though, it's a fascinating area of HK that you might not visit unless staying at this hotel.

<Content>Fantastic, Can't wait to go back The hotel was marvellous. Would definately recommend upgrading to the club lounge, we had 8 women travelling and it was a great place to stay. <Author>h1st0ry
<Content>A cut above the norm I was a little sceptical at the rave reviews that this hotel got from Trip Advisor reviewers as they seemed too good to be true. However, having stayed there for two nights in September 2007, I would endorse the positive comments that have been written about Langham Place. The staff seemed to go out of their way to be courteous and friendly. In particular, the concierge staff in the lobby were very helpful in providing information about diferent locations in Hong Kong and how to get there. The rooms are beatifully furnished and equipped and are a cut above those of the average large hotel in this class. It is worth asking for a room with a view as some floors provide better views than others. My friends and I had booked two rooms, one of which had stunning views while the view in the other was far less spectacular. The mezannine bar is very pleasant and reasonably priced, at least during the early evening happy hour. Room service was efficient and of a good standard. There is a swimming pool (and spa) on the top floor with great views over the city. It is a really pleasant place to go in the evening or early in the morning. The hotel is also in a great location within walking distance of the top end of Nathan Street and very close to the metro station. It is linked physically to a shopping mall which mainly caters for a clientele of under 25s but has some good cheapish restaurants. The hotel is also within walking distance of the night market in Temple Street although much that is on sale is scarcely worth the effort. I had been in Hong Kong before about seven years ago and was surprised at how few bargains are to be had now. Beijing provides much better opportunities for the enthusiastic shopper! My only quibble with the hotel was that my room was not serviced until 4.00 pm which was very late. At 3.00 pm I asked at reception as well as the staff on the floor that it be done as soon as possible. I was, however, a little surprised that none of the staff seemed to think it unusual that the room was not cleaned in the morning. It slightly spoiled a good day in Hong Kong that I came back to find my room as I had left it early in the morning. Nonetheless, I would strongly recommend this hotel and will defintely stay there when I am back in Hong Kong.  
<Date>Oct 20, 2007

<Author>luvtotravelnasia
<Content>My favorite in Hong Kong I've stayed here over 20 times and every time I love it even more! The rooms are fantastic, especially the corner rooms and the blissful bed is the best! The portal work and play lounge on the 2nd floor is a great place to have a drink after work and the rooftop pool and hot tub are some of the best in Hong Kong! The gym and spa are also first rate. My absolute favorite part of this hotel, however, is the dinner buffet. I've never eaten more oysters in my life...simply delicious! The service is always good from the moment you arrive to the moment you check out and I actually like the location better than TST or HK Island as it give you a chance to get out and experience the real Hong Kong. Also its easy to get from the hotel to anywhere in the territory via the MRT or KCR...the only negative is that there is no shuttle bus from the Airport Express Kowloon station to the Langham Place. There is no place I'd rather stay in Hong Kong!

<Author>Portuguesemanowar
<Content>Did exactly what it said on the tin As you may have already gathered from the multitude of glowing write ups on this hotel it is absolutely tremendous. The whole experience from initial booking to final check out was excellent. As many people have already said we found the best rate on the hotels own web site, there was also the opportunity to book breakfasts at a significant discount, paying as you dine can be pricey. There is also the opportunity to Skype the hotel through their web site to sort out and queries/problems you may have. Just prior to arrival we received a welcome email informing us of what offers were available, which was nice touch. Our family room was fantastic on the 32nd floor. Great views of Hong Kong and the bed was indeed blissful. The room was excellently equipped and the mini bar had a good variety of drinks at a reasonable price. The pool area is superbly located on the roof of the hotel with excellent panoramic views of Hong Kong. The Chuen Spa provides virtually every type of massage and treatment available and is well worth a visit. Many people have commented on the surrounding area of the hotel being a bit dodgy, but I think that it what makes the Langham even more special. Busy street markets just round the corner, the Langham Place mall accessible via a covered walkway, much cheaper breakfast alternatives exist in here as well, and the MTR are only 5 mins from your room. My family and I never felt threatened once whilst in Hong Kong. Perhaps the Langham鈥檚 biggest plus point are it鈥檚 superb staff. Everyone of them has obviously been well trained, as from the door staff to the management I came into contact with, they were polite, helpful and extremely proud to be of service. The breakfast buffet selection was excellent with all the food of a high standard. Complementary internet is available on the 6th and via the TV in your room for a daily tariff. I would strongly recommend that anyone visiting Hong Kong try the Langham Place Hotel as it is fantastic.

<Author>Zaina
<Content>An outstanding hotel with great amenities and comfort! I stayed at The Langham Place in Hong Kong with my family for 12 nights (20/8-1/9/07). We had one Residence Suite and two standard rooms.Our stay was just wonderful. The rooms were beautifully fitted with everything one needs. It鈥檚 a fairly new hotel with high tech features and flat wall TV鈥檚 (the room phone had a screen which allows you to access news, weather, information..etc). The beds and pillows were superbly comfortable. The breakfast buffet was grand with an amazing variety of foods. In the suite, we had access to the Club Lounge, which is open 24 hrs and offered a relaxing atmosphere where you can enjoy free internet, coffee and drinks anytime (plus snacks in the afternoon and evenings). The Club Lounge is only open to suites and club room guests. However, free internet is also provided at the bar level (above the lobby) to all guests. The hotel also has magnificent spa facilities (called the Chuan Spa) 鈥?something not to be missed. The treatments were costly but indeed splendid and worth it. The hotel also has a top floor covered pool with breathtaking city views, saunas and exercise gym. The location was ideal. The hotel is directly connected to a shopping mall with lots of places to eat and to the Mong Kong MTR underground station.It's one of those hotels which you would really be hard pressed to find something wrong with it.The staff we met throughout our stay were very friendly and helpful, except for one little blemish that occurred at our check out from the suite. At 2PM, I was sitting at the Club Lounge desk waiting to check out while a male employee was finishing up some paperwork. As soon as he finished, I expected him to attend to me because I had been the only person sitting right in front of him, across his desk, for some time. But instead, he noticed a Chinese looking man, holding a US passport, entering the Club Lounge. He immediately got up and went around the desk to greet him, asking him if he was checking in or out. He then proceeded to help him, while totally ignoring me. Favoritism, racism, something else鈥?I don鈥檛 know! But whatever it was鈥? it was a blatantly rude behavior. Anyway, another female employee, who happened to be in the Lounge speaking to another guest came later to the desk and helped me check out. Despite this last minute disappointing flop, I still highly rate this hotel and give it the full five stars which it rightfully deserves.

<Author>CitiesTraveller
<Content>No way it is no 1 in Hong Kong We stayed in the hotel on Thursday night in a standard deluxe room before heading out to Macau the next day and back again for a night stay in an executive room (much bigger). Location is good, lots of shops and just a short walk to the MTR. It is easy to get to the hotel from the airport by taking the A21 express bus which cost us HK$33 per person. The standard deluxe room is small and definitely look nicer on the website. Service is efficient but the front desk staff not very smooth in handling the check-in. Try too hard to sell the executive room but we relented the second night by paying HK$200 extra.For travellers who do not like crowds, then this hotel is not for him or her as the place are pretty crowded with lots of people at the street level.Why I've said that this hotel cannot be No 1 is that it does not broadcast English Premier League (a must nowadays for sports fans). Overall think the hotel is alright but will choose to stay at Hong Kong island hopefully to avoid the crowds.

<Author>flora5
<Content>Great location This 5 star hotel is in the middle of all the shopping action. It's a 5 minute walk to the local markets and you're next door to the very classy Langham Place Shopping Plaza. Royal Plaza, another great shopping complex, is a 10 minute walk away. You'll pass Fa Yuen St if you head in that direction, that too is a great place to shop for bargains. The hotel is also next door to a MTR. It is in a busy area of Mongkok but if you plan to shop then this is a great place to stay. There are also lots of places to eat near by, especially in the Langham Place Shopping Plaza. The Langham Place Hotel has a great buffet breakfast, worth the extra payment and the views from our 25th floor were fabulous. We paid a little extra for an executive room, got a good deal from their website. The room was small, but who needs a big room when you are out most of the time? The marble bathroom was excellent with a deep bath. The bed too was comfortable with many pillows to choose from. We had internet access and a reliable room safe. The staff were great too and English is spoken well. I don't have anything negative to say, we had a great 4 night stay.
