<Author>piccolita
<Content>overrated!!!! While i think this place probably deserves to be in the top twenty of Hong Kong, I don't quite get the number one ranking here- its exaggerated! I booked the Langham Place in HK precisely because of the reviews it got here at tripadvisor (sucker! :P) but if i were to return, i would feel indifferent about returning to this hotel.Things i liked that probably makes its ranking on the high side:* Good concierge service for restaurant reservations. The guy was not able to get us a table at the restaurant we wanted on the exact day we wanted, but we truly did appreciate his effort on getting back to us with an alternate date and time. Then he even left messages for us to remind us of this reservation. Nice.* Room service was also good. Very courteous and prompt and they get the details right. Yummy burger and fries, i might add.* Basically they got the smart phone thing right. Everytime you picked up the phone for a question, to order food, or for any requests, they were very polite in answering, helpful with any questions, and they would act on request or order immediately. The people were well trained in this area.* Although the size of the bathroom is small-ish, the bathroom experience was very pleasant with a separate tub and shower and there were two shower options, the rain like one thats above the head, and the hand held one. Toiletries smell yummy.* Conveniently located near an MTR station, no need to go outdoors. This was really good since it was raining while we were there. (But since I dont have business in the Mongkok area, am not sure I'd stay here again). Still better to stay at Tsim Sha Tsui area, Central, Causeway or even Wanchai, so you're in between Central and Causeway Bay.* the iHome was a nice touch :)Now about the not so desirable things:-the Langham Patrolman. This guy in the lobby who makes it his job to see if anybody in the lobby is misbehaving. Im serious, I think this is really his job. I had to wait in the lobby since room wasnt ready, so i go to the mall and get myself a coffee and look around. I returned to hotel and it was still too early, so I just sit there in one of the chairs which has a table beside it. I put my coffee on the table and start searching for something in my bag. Then.... Mr Langham Police comes and says, Sorry, but you arent allowed to put down your coffee at the table. that was really bizarre... I thought that was what tables were for!!! So i ask why? And he says with a really apologetic face, I really dont know but those are the rules. Sheeesh, if that was his job and he had to do it everyday, he might as well know why, right?? Ok that was not an isolated case. On a separate occasion, sitting in the lobby again, this guy was reprimanded for sitting on the arm part of the chair, since there werent enough chairs. And on another occasion, there was this lady beside me who was sort of filling her nails. Now this is really weird, filing your nails in public. But apparently, she broke her nail, so it was sort of necessary at that time. And of course Langham Patrol guy comes and tells her that filing is not allowed. And she says, but i broke my nail, and he says, can i see?? So bizarre. This lobby police thing is really a first for me, and its really weird. They make you uncomfortableon your own holiday.-I have to agree with the other guy that the check-in service is not quite good. First off you are welcomed at street level by these girls in hot pink outfit, and pink hats. I am not sure if I could blame my mood upon arrival, but it was just a tad annoying that they tried to make chit chat which i found a little bit contrived, like it was all a part of a script or something. GOing back to check-in, we arrived almost noon time, so this could be the reason that the queue felt like a bank queue, seriously. I mean standing in line isnt exactly jolly when you've had just come from a flight. There were probably three lanes and in each lane there were about three persons in line. Then when it was my turn to check in, the lady in the unapollogetically told me that we had to wait until two pm to get the room. It wasnt her fault really that check in time is really at 2, but it didnt help either that she had a look that felt like she just wanted to get me over with and get to the next person in line.-Room size: tiny. The size is similar to European style hotel rooms. For Hong Kong standard this is really small. No need for a huge plasma tv really, as the bed is close to the wall in front. Room had 2 single beds. There's really no option to get 2 double beds in room since they dont have any.All in all, market place-like check-in experience plus Langham police guy really ruined it for me. I am not sure this is a five star hotel. Probably a four star yes. If you feel the need to stay in Mongkok or have business there, then this is probably the best option there is. Otherwise, there are so many other options in HK. By the way, another reviewer mentioned he paid USD95 per room per night. At this price, i think its worth it. In the end, i think the level of enjoyment comes relative to price paid, so since i paid more here, and couldve paid less at similar level, better situated hotels, my satisfaction level is only at 80% level.

Also on the 2nd day, because of this mix up, we came back to find the room not serviced after leaving the room for a full day. Not 5 star service. Breakfast was quite nice but I wouldnt mind if they had a bit more selection. The rooms were small but had everything you would expect and a few nice tech gadgets. There are a lot of lobby atendants dressed in pink to direct you inside the hotel which is good because the hotels is quite busy. The concierge was helpful and fluent in english. The whole hotel design is quite nice and classy.

<Content>A room with a view to die for.....! My husband, son and myself arrived expecting the very best-we were not disappointed. This hotel was chosen carefully for the reviews, situation, room views of Hong Kong island and proximity to shops and cultural visits. The rooms-even whilst having a bath, you can look right at over the Hong Kong skyline! I cannot describe how hypnoptic and compelling this view was-day and night-we left the curtains open all the time! I have never slept in a more comfortable bed and the room was well equipped and serviced. We ate breakfast-huge and varied array for all tastes, cultures-worth being adventurous! The hotel is perfectly situated-shopping mall attached, transport networks 2/3 minutes away, local 7/11 stores for wines (expensive in comparison to GB, beers etc-hotel prices high as you would expect). There are loads of places to eat nearby. The elevator girls are delightful in their pink costumes. The roof top pool-views-what can I say! The spa is so clean, relaxing and fully equipped-all needs pampered. Imagine a Gym overlooking Hong Kong-42nd floor-treadmills are never this exciting in GB!We had no delays check-in or out. All very efficient-excellent. We all agreed that this was an amazing hotel and it made the holiday. We are not always so impressed-would go back tomorrow-alas another year of saving up to go on holiday!! ENJOY-we did! FIBILL

<Author>Paul-Portugal
<Content>One of my all time favourite hotels I travel a lot for business  the quality of the Hotel makes a big difference to me. I really like the Langham Place and in comparison to the Hotels in HK Island or TST, think it is excellent value. The Hotel is brand spanking new and has a fresh contemporary feel to it without being boutique like. The rooms and facilities are really excellent, the MTR is a short walk so you can be anywhere in the area pretty quickly. I love the service (I think they pay people to stand around  smile !!) and the spa is wonderful (albeit a bit expensive)Only downside is that Mongkok itself is quite run down so apart from the Langham Place mall and the local markets you tend to spend 30 minutes on the MTR or in a Taxi going to the usual haunts like TST or Central.TIPS1) Buy an Octupus card, which is a pre-paid card upon which you load credit, it makes using public transport a breeze !2) Like all Hotels, the breakfast, while good, is expensive. I usually go to the nearby Mall where there is a Delifrance and Starbucks just across the walkway from the Hotel. 3) Taxi drivers don't all have good English  this Hotel seems less well known the some of the other more established ones. So you really need a card from the Hotel concierge with the name written in Chinese characters to ensure you get back !I always try to stay there when in HK  always enjoy the experience.

<Author>bigbird2423
<Content>Deserves #1 ranking on Tripadvisor I am originally from Hong Kong and have family there. As a result, I've been back a number of times and know the Hong Kong area and its hotels quite well. We stayed for a week and a half and our experience was that Langham Place is a 5 star hotel. The service that we experienced was very high and they pay attention to details. For instance, they even put your slippers in just the right place in the right direction so that you're feet slip into them as you get out of bed. The hotel room is a fairly standard size for Hong Kong (which means a little small for Hong Kong by Western standards) but has a very comfortable, firm bed, plasma TV, internet phone, and tasteful decor. The rooftop pool is fully serviced and sometimes overstaffed. There is a nice spa, sauna, men's and women's lockers and club lounge. The location in MongKok is excellent if you want a taste of a local area in Hong Kong. Essentially all of the other 5 star hotels are clustered in Tsim Sha Tsui (a nice area but a tourist district) and Central (the financial district). The hotel is connected to a 13 story shopping mall (Langham Place Mall) that has many restaurants, shops and a movie theater. The hotel is also connected to the MongKok subway station. You can get to the mall or the subway via skybridge and the escalators without going outside. The concierge was helpful and everyone was beyond cordial. The pink elevator ladies are a nice touch. Because there are so many great restaurants to try in the MongKok area, I would suggest limiting dining inside the hotel. The restaurants inside the hotel are good but they are much more expensive than the surrounding restaurants. Try Guongzhou Garden inside the mall instead if you want top notch Cantonese service and food. Note that we paid about the equivalent of $90 (US dollars) per night due to a promotion by Cathay Pacific and purchased this through a Chinese travel agency in the United States. This is obviously a great deal but in general, the standard prices are still significantly lower than prices at 5 star hotels in Tsim Sha Tsui or Central. Everyone treated us well and we tipped the front desk and the concerige at our first contact with them (check-in). This can sometimes enhance the experience even at a good hotel.

<Author>AmeeLondon
<Content>Simply the best place to stay in Hong Kong! Stayed at the Langham Place Hotel in Mongkok for five nights with my elderly parents on a business-cum-pleasure trip to Hong Kong. Thus I am able to testify that this is an excellent hotel to stay at, either for work or for play.Paid for a Kowloon room with triple accommodation, which consists of a giant King sized bed, and a single bed, both extremely comfortable. The pillow menu is a nice touch, but hardly neccessary, as there were already three types of pillow provided as standard.Bathroom is extremely well-stocked. For the triple room, you don't get the clear glass partition that others appear to get with doubles - which was good for us, as my parents are not exactly liberal!The extra I paid to get access to the facilities in the lounge on the 36th floor is a good investment. It is a good place to relax, and there seems to be a constant supply of snacks and drinks (including cocktails) on tap. My father loved the message chair, which afforded relief for sore feet while offering an amazing view of the HK skyline. It is also easier to arrange to settle the bill and check out via the reception desk there, as the one in the lobby can be busy.The services at the hotel is impeccable, and I agree with previous reviewers, that the lobby and concierge services are friendly, warm and extremely welcoming. We never had to wait very long for anything, as everything was delivered extremely quickly, efficiently and with a smile.We preferred breakfast on the ground floor (as opposed to the lounge) as there was greater variety. Selection was pretty standard for 5* hotels (multinational cuisine). Services of the serving staff there could be variable, depending on where you sit and how busy they are. The hotel appears to be popular with foreign toursts, and we (ethnically Chinese) appeared to be in the minority!The hotel is situated in the middle of Mongkok, supposedly one of the most densely populated area in the world. Nevertheless, this is exactly what we loved to do - mingle with the locals and sampling the hussle and bustle of everyday life - so don't pick this location if you like a peaceful and quiet stroll! Access to other parts of Hong Kong were also extremely easy by the MTR via the mall next door - got to a wedding reception in Central on time without any problems, during a typhoon number 8 alert!I would highly recommend this hotel to anyone. The price may be on the top end, but I felt it was worth every single penny.

<Author>CMinch
<Content>Great Location Firstly, Thankyou all who wrote revies of this hotel, as it helped me choose this great hotel to stay at for 4 nights. We stayed at the hotel, whilst re-locating back from the UK to Australia, and in need of a rest....with a 2 yr old child. We booked directly with the hotel, and also arranged a shuttle bus from the airport to the hotel and vice versa. This was a great move, considering the luggage we had (Which would not of fit in a taxi) and for 180 each was not bad.The hotel itself was beautiful, and luxurious. The hotel was as described by other reviewers, and the room was big. We were upgraded to a club room (We choose not to go with the extras to have the actual club privledges - just the room). We were on the 35th floor (Which was a bit eary), but none the less had a good size room with a large bed. We choose not to get a cot for our 2 yr old, and had him in bed with us as there was plenty of room in the King sized bed for him. One complaint I had was that we arrived at 1am in the morning, and I asked where I could go for some Milk for my child. I was told we will arrange room service to deliver this to you. As I was tired I said ok, it might cost a bit, but I was curious why they did not suggest the 7-11 across the road. None the less a small glass of milk was delivered and I was charged 35 hong kong which is about 3 UK pounds. I complained the next morning and was given a credit for this, but it is something to be careful of.The location of the hotel was excellent. The hotel connects directly to the Langham shopping centre, where there is a great food hall where we ate dinner most nights. It was fun eating there as its the Chinese way and very cheap rather than eating in restaurants. The hotel was walking distance to the night markets and the Ladies market. Both places were great, and we did manage to spend quite a lot on the bargains at both markets....especially on hand-bags be a certain French designer. It is funny when they grab you and show you the catalogue for the bags....I guess what the markets are all about :-)The Metro station was close, and we went to Disneyland from there as well as downtown. It was cheap to use and efficient and cooler than walking in the ridiculous heat we were in in July. Disneyland was ok, I think the fact it was soooo hot spoilt it for us, but you cant blame the park for the whether. That said the park is reasonably small compared to other Disneylands, but still its a Disney at the end of the day.Overall the hotel is a great location, high quality and standard. It was pricey in my opinion, especially when tax and service are added to your hotel room rate. That said, I would stay again at the hotel, as its location location location.

<Content>Another good review Spent three nights at the hotel at the end of a quick trip around the region. Maybe it was to make room for the separate shower in the bathroom? Blissful bed is not quite there according to my princess daughter who wondered where they managed to get such a hard pillow top matress. But it was the best one we found in the region. Pool was fine and needed after a long day sighseeing. View from pool area on roof is fantastic. Service was fine in the hotel (though still trying to work out what job Eunice the other hatted ladies have in the lobby except to push elevator buttons) and I think it is a great base for a visit to Hong Kong. The Ladies Market is two mins away and the MTR downstairs. Food court in next door mall is a great way to get a cheap quick meal although gets very busy. Mall also had a good selection of teenage clothes in a Trendz section so for someone like me dragging a daughter around was a great choice to keep her busy.

<Author>Zoophoria
<Content>It is simple why it is No 1 on Trip advisor We stayed here for a week in Mongkok. This is on the Kowloon side and Mogkok means busy corner - and it certainly is - you get a real bustle for the city.As for the room, it was fantastic - a very complete package - you can view the TV from the bath tub even!The bed was listed as a blissful bed - and it certainly was that. There is also a pillow menu to pick your own pillows.As for the location, it is part of the Langham Place Mall which is linked to Mongkok MRT station - so you can get across very quickly - HK$5 one way to TST in Kowloon. It is right in the heart of the Chinese market - so it gets very busy especially in the evening - certainly not for people who want serenity - but watching the bustle below mixing with the neon signs a la Blade Runner is a sight to seeThe staff are friendly ans corteous and ever ready to help - the Club Lounge is fantastic and well worth having for free drinks, continental breakfast and cocktails throught the day/night.Overall, it's been No 1 here on trip advisor - the other hotels have a bit of catching up to do

<Author>Heiner5
<Content>Great hotel, great location, great lounge We stayed in Langham Place over the holy week in a 3 bed room Suite in the Club Floor. We had a twin room and a room with an extra bed. The rooms were spacious enough to commemorate us well. The extra bed was a little short but pretty comfortable. The big flat screen TV sets in both rooms were a nice feature too. Beside a nice and well lit bathroom with shower, bathtub and toilet we had another toilet room in the suite which was very well received being a party of 3. The rooms had a view over Kowloon rather than Hongkong Island but it was pretty impressive nevertheless.I really liked the Club Floor lounge which had a good selection of drinks and snacks all day long. Also there were three computers with internet access and printers for us to use for free.The restaurant was a little disappointing, so-so dinner for quite expensive prices. Breakfast was great though, large selections ranging from continental, British, Japanese to Chinese. The foodcourt and restaurants of the adjoining Langham Mall were the better choice for dinner or lunch. Through the Mall located in Mongkok you also have access to the Metro bringing you to Hongkong Island.Overall I can recommend this Hotel for business and leisure and will go there again for my next trip to HK.

<Author>kenbell
<Content>Location, Location, Location My family consisting of my husband, 2 children (8  6) and my mother stayed here for 8 days. What a fabulous location. What more could you ask for a huge shopping centre adjoing the hotel, MTR at the bottom of the shopping centre. The excitment and fantastic shopping of Mongkok just outside the doors!!! The beds were extremely confortable (especially when we had stayed a few nights earlier in our trip at another hotel and the bed was like an ironing board). We had booked 1 residence suite which consisted of a small kitchen/lounge with separate King bed and adjoining to the suite was a club room with a queen bed. Being on the club floor is sure worth the little extra upgrade cost. It is so relaxing to be able to come back after a busy day shopping or sightseeing and being able to kick back and watch the most wonderful views from the 36th floor with a wonderful glass of red. The children were most welcome in the club as we have experienced at different hotels where children are not permitted into the club....!!!! This is something that I alway now check with. All in all if you are staying in HK this is definately my pick.

<Author>thusly
<Content>Fabulous Hotel Beautifully appointed hotel common areas and room. Stayed on the Clublevel that provided quality meals (full breakfast, tea for lunch, andvarious snacks at other times) and drinks (a variety of wines, soft drinks, expresso machine, alcohol) from 6:30AM to 11PM. Free internetand computer usage at Club, as well as 2 massage chairs. Club facilities are also first rate - very comfortable, spacious, and generally quite (with the exception of noisy Americans!) Quality of the room and hotel was very high quality; room amenities include a very comfortable bed, Plasma TV, soft towels and bedding, modern bathwith tub and shower, and robes. I was upgraded to a studio - I believe room #s XX01 are those - that had fabulous views of the Hong Kong island and building skyline, as well as Kowlooon penisula and bay. Room appointments are all first rate and worthy of a five star quality rating.Room service - all good quality, reasonable prices considering. Ceasar salad disappointing, as was the hamburger (not sure what sort of meat was used). Tomato soup and noodle soups were very good and reasonable.Spa/gym faciilities are excellent - also included as part of the clublevel surcharge - modern exercise equipment with many treadmills, ellipticals and a few bikes. Weights include free weights and machines - all of very good quality. Exercise facility has lots of natural light with excellent views of the city. Spa facilities were moderately spacious, very clean and included dry and wet sauna, as well as soaking pool. Pool area was a bit small, but provided nice contrast to hustle and bustle of the city. Sort of difficult to sunbathe, due to building design.I had originally planned to stay one night to recover from a 21 day trip of China - I ended up staying three more nights and rarely left the hotel. The hotel made a great finish to my trip. Highly recommended.

<Author>wil888
<Content>Love this hotel I visit Hong Kong about 3-4 times a year and usually stay at the Conrad. I decided to give this hotel a try as they had a special deal for suites and I am so glad I did. The rate I paid was cheaper than a regular room at the Conrad (although they always upgrade me to the Executive floor, being a HHonors Diamond). I had a Residence Suite and it's actually a sitting room with full kitchen and a bedroom. The Grohe fixtures in the bathroom were very nice and I certainly appreciate the big (46 inch?) plasma televisions in both rooms. The only complaint I had was the bedroom was a little on the small side but the choice of pillows was certainly a nice touch and the mattress was nice and firm. I like to watch TV in bed and was surprised to note that the TV did not have a timer switch. The service was excellent and all the staff I came into contact with were very helpful. I love the location as I enjoy walking around Mongkok and Hong Kong being hot and humid in June, it was so nice to be able to duck back into the hotel for a quick shower and change of clothing everytime I got hot and sweaty. I already made the reservation for my trip in the Fall and I hope they continue the Suite deal next year.

<Author>Nevetson-Spice
<Content>Beautiful hotel, fantastic service This is a beautiful hotel with fantastic service and a really convenient location. We hadn't booked the executive / club package but were given a room upgrade as the hotel was full. We were persuaded to pay a supplement to upgrade to the club package to give us access to the club lounge - beer  wine available through the day plus spirits  champagne for a couple of hours each evening. There are great snacks available and an excellent complimentary breakfast. In honesty I wouldn't pay the supplement next time as the rest of the hotel is so luxurious  fabulous that it's not really necessary and I also found the club lounge a bit lacking in atmosphere.Our room on the 36th floor was amazing - the views over the city are just incredible  the clear glass wall between bedroom  bathroom means that you can enjoy the view from the shower!You can get to the MTR (underground) station via the walkway to the mall or turn left out of the hotel then first right which we found a bit quicker although either way is only a couple of minutes. The MTR service is superb - you're never more than 5 minutes from a station and the longest we ever waited for a train was 3 minutes. You should definitely buy an Octopus card to make your travel really easy. You can use the card on the underground, on buses, on the star ferry, at 7-11s and at drinks dispensers in the stations so it's really convenient  great value.

<Author>a12548
<Content>My detailed review of this fine hotel I stayed here for 6 nights and was impressed. As our airport limo wasnearing the hotel at night, we were a little worried at how the Mong Kok area looked and wondered if we made a mistake, but the next day we explored and felt totally safe. Just keep away from the west side of hotel (Reclaimation St and over). Some say the hotel is out of theway, but it makes up for it with the Langham Place mall attached and also a MTR station downstairs which has you minutes away from Tsim Sha Tsui, HK island etc. Subways are spotless and I know the routes rather well by now. The Ladies Market is kinda trashy, low class vendors bracing for bargaining. As I walked past several stalls I canhear the vendors actually yelling at the tourists if they couldnt close the deal. I bought a Swiss watch, which worked for a day, when the maid empties the trash can, I hope she doesnt think it works. Save your shopping for Nathan rd. The Bird Market, hmmm stay away..when we were in hotel we heard on news they shut it down because a bird was infected with bird flu, this was June 16th. They showed the health people spraying the area and the shop owners were livid, screaming about the closings. Dont chance it. All other surrounding streets spark the senses, interesting to see one of the most crowded areas in the world pulsate. We wanted to see a HK horserace so we took the KCR rail to Sha Tin Racecourse. It was an awesome experience, not like the USA tracks. There wasnt cursing, spitting, throwing programs or yelling. It was orderly and really a pretty track. From Langham take the Mong Kok KCR to dedicated Racecourse stop..which was about 14 minutes away. Bring your passport for free admission, we sprung for the Members Club which was air conditioned, well worth it. If you like Malls, Times Square is the best, take MTR to causeway bay and exit at Times square ramp. The pavilion is picture perfect. You must do the Peak, and eat at The Lookout, reserve for a table looking over the city. We went forbreakfast and it was almost empty. We did the HK sponsered Tai Chi classes offered at the Museum of Art near the Star ferry in Tsim Sha Tsui. The instructor was fantastic, really into his Tai Chi, many locals were there as volunteers. The Canton Rd mall and shops were kinda pricy and dont have that HK feel. Also visit the Temple on Nathan Rd about 5 minute walk north of Police Station. Dont choke on the incense smoke, it is overbearing but its an experience watching the locals give their offerings. Respect their privacy, no photos, however they allowed us to take pics if people werent in pic. I can go on forever, I love Hong Kong. My only donts are the Ladies Market and Bird Market. The Langham Mall has great food choices on 4th floor, actually quite cheap for good food. Oh another 'dont'...I wouldnt eat from those vendors with the meat and squid out in open, I saw several instances where they handled the food and touched theirfaces, dirty water etc. Well, I got off track, this was supposed to be a hotel review, its great, the 5th floor work/play area..free internet and a bar with superb eats, kinda pricy. The pool is sweet and the treadmills make you feel like youre walking over the city. The breakfast was excellent, Im a Dim Sum and sushi addict and they had both. Rooms are small but we basically slept there only, so no big deal.  
<Date>Jun 21, 2007

<Author>worldtraveller68
<Content>Excellent 1 night stayover I was at the end of my 2.5 week trip through Asia, during which I had gone to Singapore to meet with my vendor, gone to Guangzhou to meet with my client, back to Singapore to get engaged (yes you read that correctly), and then to Hong Kong to meet with client. Needless to say, I was incredibly tired and just wanted a nice place to stay that was convenient.Langham Place hotel turned out to be the exact remedy I needed. For one the location in Mongkok is central, it's connected to a mall and the busy shopping area (including the infamous Ladies Night Market where it's like Thailand's Chattuchuk market but in Cantonese). The hotel was well-appointed, the bed comfortable, bathroom clean, and even though I didn't have much a view I didn't really care. It was just nice to stay in a nice place that was reasonable from a price perspective.The only regret that I had was that I couldn't use the much-talked about spa as they were fully booked. I did manage to go see the rooftop pool that's a part of the spa, and it was very impressive.Next time I'm in Hong Kong I think I might stay here as opposed to Hong Kong Island as the transportation is incredibly convenient, it's closer to the airport, and there is obviosuly a lot to do in Kowloon. However most of all, I really liked this hotel a lot and wouldn't mind coming back for a longer stay, including a few hours in the spa.

<Author>Washington206
<Content>Good - but not dazzling After spending four nights at the Langham Place hotel in Mong Kok, I was surprised to see it atop Trip Advisor's ratings for Hong Kong. It's not that the hotel has major flaws - indeed, our stay was quite pleasant - but it wasn't extraordinary either. Langham Hotels maintain two properties in Hong Kong; the Mong Kok location is a bit farther from the main tourist attractions, while the other hotel is more centrally located. Had I the chance to do it over, I would not opt for the Mong Kok location. That said, the room was clean and comfortable, the staff very helpful. The hotel is connected to a mall by a sky bridge, so there's a food court, coffee shops, and a host of stores just a few steps away. Free internet was a nice perk, too.

<Author>F12EE
<Content>One of My Favorite Hotels A little about me, I'm a college graduate with an Architecture degree and am not rich by any means and thus don't have the funds to stay at hotels of a luxurious sort and though I have been fortunate enough to stay at some pretty suave hotels in my short life The Langham Place was simply one of the best. Though I would have preferred a hotel located on the HK Island side of the harbor the location was fantastic. Getting to the hotel was a simple bus ride away from the airport and you literally do not have to go above ground to get from the MTA station to the hotel. The hotel is connected to a brand new shopping mall (with a Starbucks right outside the lobby) and the famous Mong Kok shopping markets right outside the doors. The design is hip and wonderfully fun. The hotel bar is hopping with live music at night and the spa, gym and rooftop pool are all free for hotel guests to use. The gym may not be fully equipped and I'm sorry to say I did not try paying for the full spa treatment but the rooftop pool was spectacular. The room features were wonderful and the bathroom was a design treat. Don't forget to ask for an iPod stereo if you happen to bring your iPod. And while there's free internet downstairs there's only a few computers and it's slow but to get the quick connection in your room you have to pay around $20 a night. So all in all the hotel was amazing. So much so that it was dangerous because we spent much more of our five days in Hong Kong enjoying the hotel than we would have liked to. And that's one of the biggest compliments I can give it.

<Author>Incognitosu
<Content>A great hotel to return to Stayed at Langham Place for 3 nights from 18 May in the standard twinroom. Overall, had a great experience and would definitely recommend the hotel to friends and all.Read that many before me had already gushed at length about the hotel. Nevertheless, because we had visited Hong Kong on a particularly rainy season, we really came to appreciate all the little things that make up Langham Pl.What makes Langham Pl. a great sanctuary to return to, especially after a rain-soaked day out:- the ginger flower scented lobby is a welcomed salve from the assault of your olfactory senses by the damp rain and smells of street food (the notorious smelly tofu included).- the specially created Blissful Bed rejuvenated us with restful sleep- Life can be closer to a bed of roses if you try out their wonderfully scented rose pillow from an array offered by the pillow menu.- a tub to soak your aches away and within easy reach of your fingers, a little pulley to elevate the screen shielding the glass-walled bathroom, so you can enjoy the cable offerings of the plasma TV from the comfort of your bubble bath.- connected walkway from hotel lobby to the food level of Langham Place Mall lets you grab a quick and convenient bite while keeping you dry.- the connectivity of the hotel (through the mall) to the MTR makes for convenient access and much welcomed shelter from the on pouring rain.- IP telephony gadget in room allows you to check up on the directoryof the interlinked mall so you can preview the variety of eating establishments and know exactly which outlet to head to for that crabcongee, even before you step out of the comfort of your room.- Ipod compatible sound system to dock your Ipod and wake up to your favourite tunes- nightly turn-down service that ensures your bed is ready for bedtime and that you have a bottle of water and a glass handy by yourbedside.- free 24hr internet access at the PCs/Macs available at their 5th floor should you need to check that urgent email.- concierge that speak impeccable English and are always ready to point you in the right direction with a proffered map or a hotel cardto take to your cab driver.- warm and friendly lift ladies who greet you from afar and anticipate your every need - which floor are you heading to? Do you need directions out of the hotel? While I thoroughly enjoyed my stay at Langham Place, I must say that its location may not be most ideal for everyone. While Mongkok is adored by many travelers as it鈥檚 where the lively street markets are and it adds much local colour to their stay, if you are on a tight-scheduled shopping trip however, you may prefer to stay at the Tsim Sha Tsui or Causeway Bay area - where the malls are. Especially if you are visiting Hong long for its summer sale to do some serious shopping. More quality buys can be found in the above areas, rather than the flea markets of Mong Kok. That said, Langham Pl is only a mere couple of stops away from TST and probably less than 30min MTR ride to Causeway Bay.Some may also find the standard rooms a little small. To be frank, due to space constraints, our twin beds were placed so close together, they could have been mistaken for a double-room instead! However, we don鈥檛 feel crammed in a confined space, perhaps due to the clever use of mirrored surfaces and walls to optically 鈥渆nlarge鈥?the interiors and also the much appreciated floor to ceiling windows that offer vantage views if you reside on the higher floors.Things that can help top my already enjoyable Langham Pl. experience?- management could start paying more attention to the maintenance of the bathroom. While the rest of the bathroom was immaculate, my bathtub was a tad stained and found a few stray hairs on the tub. Nothing a quick rinse of water couldn't get rid of ...but it'll be better if the guests didn't have to see them.- could do with a second set of bath toiletries for twin-share/double-room guests- really adore the ginger flower scent so would be nice if guests areoffered the option to have the same scent spritzed in their rooms as part of turn-down service... but that could just be my personal preference.....- could be less stringent on the late checkout. We could only get a complimentary late-checkout till 1pm. Anytime thereafter is subjectedto hourly charges. I've been to many hotels that could offer complimentary late checkout to 3pm at least. Although at Langham Pl. you could still head up to the spa/pool level after check out and use its facilities for freshening up.- discount on the hefty printing charges please? Was charged HKD 8 per page for printing e-tickets on level 5. gulp.

<Author>george01
<Content>Nice Hotel Stayed at the the Langham this past March. Had booked a club room, got upgraded to a club suite upon arrival. Very nice, wonderful view, a bottle of champaigne and chocolates were waiting as we were celebrating a special ocassion, on the floor check-in/out, great plasma TVs (3) in the suite, free drinks 6-8 PM I believe, free breakfast, great omelettes, just nice. The location is fascinating to say the least, in old Hong Kong. Very colorful, have to see the street market by the hotel, most everything is alive, quite an experience. As for the location, we thought it was a little far from the main attractions, since most of the action, night life, etc. is in the harbor section. However, we crisscrossed the city one day in taxis for just about $20US. Which brings me to a great experience we had with a taxi driver. We hailed it to go from the jade market to a buddist temple (we had all the destinations written in chinese by hotel staff since taxi drivers speak very little English). When pointing to the driver where we wanted to go, he saw the name and location of the hotel we were staying at thinking we wanted to go there. Ended-up leaving my eye glasses in the car, case and all. I thought for sure I'll never see them again. Wouldn't you know, the driver remembered us (we were the only westerners in that particular temple) and the hotel we were staying, and returned them when his shift was over in late afternoon. Unbelievable. Security at the hotel is pretty tight, my wife smokes, only allowed outside the hotel, and whenever she went for a cigarrette in front of the hotel she'd be assigned a door man to watch over her, and the same for other guests who went outside for a smoke. It makes you wonder about the general safety of the area. However we walked around, day time, without incident. All-in-all, had a great time in Hong Kong and at the Lamgham.  
<Date>May 18, 2007

<Author>weed39
<Content>Experience to contrast LANGHAM PLACE HOTEL MONGKOKReviewer: Member from Queensland Australia.What a vast contrast finding a 5 Star hotel situated in the New Territories market area, but this first class hotel had all the comforts of home plus lots more.We had an Executive room on the 23rd.floor-did not actually see any of the other rooms though. Had booked King Sized bed but were told on checking in this would be rectified the next day, which to their word it was.Rooms are not large, but very comfortable. Every item you would reasonably expect is in the room. Large plasma screen TV is great to view from the bed without the need to put on the specs.Room is servied twice daily, once to make up the room in the morning, the in the evening to turn back the bed and change towels if necessary. We found the room very clean. Shoe shine service is on a daily basis if required and gratis.Bathroom is quite spacious with a large shower, and has both slider hand held shower head, plus an overhead fixed shower which is great for shampooing hair.Tea and coffee facilities are in abundance and great selection of various types of teas. Japanese as well as Chinese teas, plus usual western English and breakfast teas.Restaurants are well laid out and quite spacious. Staff are very friendly, courteous and cannot do enough for you. They always greet you with a smile and thank you politely as you leave. There is a 10 per cent service charge on top of meals, but couldnt find out if it was a Goods  service tax, and accoding to what we learnt is not part of any gratuity for staff. Meals can be a little on the high side, but quite comparable with others around the Ocean terminal in the Tsim Sha Tsui area. Bath towels are very big, almost the size of a single bed blanket.Two 500 ml bottles of Bonaqua water are left in room each day-these too are free.At the entrance, and around the reception area Pink Ladies greet you as you arrive and leave the hotel, and attended to getting you into the lift. They are really terrific are so petite dressed in suits of pink with black hats, almost impish with friendly mannerisms. They won't or aren't allowed to accept tips.Although in a relatively high density living area closely resembling slums, we never felt uneasy walking around.

<Author>chiongmaya
<Content>Excellent ! Me, my wife, and my 2 kids had a wonderful stay in Langham Place Hotel in Mongkok from May 5-9, 2007. Upon arrival, we went up to the lobby which was located on the 4th floor. It was not as big and wide as I had seen in official hotel photos, but did not lose any of the glitter and elegance nonetheless. Staff was proficient in English, very attentive, and even upgraded me to an executive room. True enough, there were 2 ladies in red who will press the elevator buttons for you. The room was not big as compared to other hotels, but it is not cramped in any way. The bed was huge. 4 of us slept on it, together with 9 pillows and 2 stuffed toys which my kids brought along. I have read from a tripadvisor review before complaining about the legs of the bed. He was correct. We hurt our toes many times hitting the bed's legs. It should have been moved a little bit inward to clear our feet. Impressive was the 42 plasma tv hung on the wall, with a multitude of satellite channels to choose from. But the tv doesn't react to the remote control instantly. You have to wait for maybe 3 or 5 seconds. There was a dvd player which we never got to use.The Cisco IP phone on the office table was also a great feature. You can set up wake-up calls, check your running bill in real time, check voice messages, and sort through among a lot of useful info. There was a coffee maker with water kettle, lots of complimentary stuff like ground coffee, instant coffee, Milo chocolate drink, and a wide variety of tea. The bathroom was exactly like in the pictures I have seen before. The glass sink was so elegant. You can watch tv while inside the tub. There was a speaker in the bathroom so you can hear the tv too. I wish there was a bidet on the toilet seat as commonly found in Korean hotels. The glass wall may be very nice for honeymooners. I wish the roll down shade would be improved. There was still a gap of about an inch when the shades are down. I was surprised when I was taking a shower and the kids were laughing out loud.They were peeking as I was taking a bath!Other nice amenities were the ipod cradle, ironing board, the big safe where you can put your laptop inside as you charge, the pillow menu where you can ask for additional free pillows. We were happily surprised to have complimentary wine and chocolates because it was our 12th wedding anniversary. They are thoughtful enough to have provided an umbrella for you to use in case the weather gets bad.One of the things I thought that needed to be changed was the door closer. I do not know if it is hydraulic or spring activated, but is sure makes opening the door difficult. Should be adjusted to make the door feel lighter. Making things worse was the door knob. It did not give a good grip if you are opening the door from inside. And if you are entering the room, you'd have to lean your shoulder onto the door as you insert the key card on the main switch panel. The swimming pool on the 42nd floor was nothing grand at all, but the changing room on the 41st floor was impressive. Supplies were generous like hair gel, mouthwash, clean disinfected hair brush, shaving kits, and comb. You can even use the spinner drier to remove excess water from your bathing suit/trunks. There was a hot tub with the water maintained at 42 degrees C. I didnt try it as I felt it was too hot for me. There was a steam room as well. The elevators were inconsistent. Sometimes, it was instantly ready. Sometimes, we had to wait for at least 3 minutes to get a ride down to the lobby. After 11pm, you must have your card key with you to activate the elevator. You'll have to insert the card, then pull it out after a few seconds, then the buttons will work. And there was a tv screen in the elevator showing black  white movies from half a century ago. In my opinion, it would have been better if it just shows news bulletins pertinent to guests, like weather reports or CNN. If you like to try authentic Hong Kong cuisine that is not expensive, there is a cooked food market just beside the hotel along Shanghai Road. Take the escalators up and it is a dining hall with around 15 kiosks selling a variety of authentic HK meals. Cheap at HK$12 a meal. There was not a single English menu in sight, but I tried kiosk # 12 and I was surprised that the lady there spoke English well. She explained to me all her menu. If you like roast meats on rice, try the outlets along Argyle corner Shanghai, which is just a stone's throw away. 7-11 and KFC and Watson's are all nearby. McDonald's is across Nathan but is just about 8 minutes walk. There is a money changer nearby, just behind the hotel, along Shanghai Street near the corner of Argyle. But still, those inside Chungking Mansion in TST give the best rate. If you cant go to TST for the money changers, there are 2 changers along Soy Street between Portland and Nathan that have good rates also. One of the advantages of this hotel is the proximity to Sai Yeung Choi street that sells a lot of electronic goods, Fa Yuen Street that sells rubber shoes, and Tung Choi Street which is the Ladies Market. All shops in these streets open till at least 11pm, some even till midnight. MTR station is also around the corner. Before leaving, there was a feedback form which I filled out. There were 2 pencils in the room, and both of them broke their tips immediately. A hotel of this status should use better pens/pencils. Generally, i find this hotel much much better than most hotels I have stayed in. The pros outweigh the cons. I will surely come back to this hotel when I visit HK again.

If you like a lot of fresh fruit for breakfast, you will be disappointed- mainly tinned fruit. But the omelettes were goodLocation wise, for mixing with locals and easy accessibility to the main tourist sites, this is the hotel for you. If you want to spend your time clubbing and getting pissed, stay on the island (please!).

<Author>sbj
<Content>What An Experience Wow, where to begin ?We stayed for four nights in a Langham Suite and our final night in the Chuan Infinity Suite, each with access to the Langham Hotel Club executive facility.Firstly the rooms. The Langham Suite was lovely. It has a large lounge and fully equipped kitchenette. The super-king bed is incredibly comfortable and the bathroom has a separate bath and excellent shower. As mentioned in other reviews it also has a glass wall to the bedroom, with mechanised screens. The room also has large flat screen TVs and dvd players in lounge and bedroom, wireless broadband and floor to ceiling windows overlooking Kowloon.The Chuan Infinity Suite is something else. It is incredibly luxurious. The whole room is done immaculately in dark wood and again has two large TVs, internet etc. and also console controlled ambient lighting and music. The real attraction of this room though is the bathroom. It contains a lovely infinity bath with hydrotherapy and chromotherapy, plus separate toilet, shower room and steam room ! The photos on the web site do not do it justice.The service that we received from the hotel and the club facility was amazing. They were incredibly friendly and brought out special vegetarian food for my wife every evening that we were there. One of the waiters even took a trip out to a local market to buy a whole range of vegetarian meat substitute dishes and served this to us one evening with a range of vegetables. In every respect, the staff went above and beyond the call of duty.The spa and the treatments were amazing too 鈥?highly recommended.The location of the hotel on Kowloon is fine. It is very close to the city MTR underground system (depending on how you navigate the journey) meaning that you can quickly get to most places in the city. It is also on the doorstep of the more traditional markets too.All in all, I cannot recommend the Langham Place hotel highly enough. I honestly don鈥檛 think I can find anything to improve on.

<Author>Dagindi
<Content>My new favorite hotel in Hong Kong!!! Let me start off by saying I have been going to HK for almost 20 years. I have stayed at the Regent (Now the intercontinental), the Harbour Plaza(s), as well as the Sheraton, Nikko, Shangri La, and a few others.This hotel is located in Mong Kok which is 3 stops from Tsim Sha Tsui (waterfront area) on the MTR (Subway).Side note - The best way to get around HK is using the MTR. It's clean, safe, and super effecient. Takes a little getting used too but the transit authority has made it so user friendly that you wont want to move around HK any other way.I have always been partial to the Harbour Plaza because it was Regent Quality  Service at Sheraton prices. Please see my last review on the Harbour Plaza and why I went in search of a new hotel and I am so glad I did.If your a first time visitor to HK I do NOT reccomend you stay here only because I firmly belive there is nothing more spectacular then a Harbour View room in Hong Kong. There is nothing more spectacular then waking up and seeing the busting Victoria Harbour.That said this hotel is perfect for every stay after your first. The service is second to non in all of HK. From the second you arrive to till you leave the staff is there to please.For the first two nights I stayed in a standard room. The room is fine. The only knock is the bed is very firm but not Chinese firm so its livable.The first night I ordered room service. I wasnt that hungry so i ordered an appitizer. The app was HUGE. I couldnt even finish it.The next 3 nights I stayed in an executive suite and I have to tell you that it was one of the best suites I ever stayed in. Nice living room with a full kitchen, (who knew they even existed in HK?!?!?). Awesome shower and bathroom plus fantastic flat screen plazmas in every room (2 in the suites).Wireless internet was a great plus! The added value of breakfast, snacks, and drinks on the exec level club is well worth it. Every morning I had breakfast (made to order eggs!!) on the exec level, followed by afternoon snacks, and night caps. The view from the exec lounge is awesome. Since this is one of the taller hotels in HK you really get a cool birds eye view of the Mong Kok. Not interested in Hotel food, take the enclosed walk way to the Langham Place shopping center (off the lobby) and when you enter the mall you will see at least 10 resturants too choose from plus Starbuck and little gourmet shops. The mall is nice to walk around, plus you can get to the MTR without every having to go outside!!.The hotel is almost 4 years old, but the staff acts like its brand new and try so hard to make sure your stay is as comfortable as possible. I really enjoyed my stay here and looked forward to coming back to my room each day/night. A great example of the service is during my first two nights I stayed in a standard room on the 8 floor, my next 3 nights I was on the 38th floor. The response time to my requests were identical.Oh I almost forgot!! Each room is equipped with the S.M.A.R.T. Phone. In most hotels you have to dial a certain extension to reach a certain department such as room service or bell hop. At the Langham Place, all you do is press 0 (zero) and the person that answers takes care of everything for you from room service, housekeeping, bell hop, resevations, anything. Its having the concierge at your beck and call with the push of one button. You dont realize how awesome that is until you have it.Great hotel, great location, great food, great service...great great great great!!I will not stay anywhere else in HK!!!!

<Author>johncharles
<Content>Location, location The best thing for us was the location. Mongkok is as Chinese as it gets in Hong Kong. The extensive night market five minutes walk away has far more local shoppers than tourists. Buses and trains are on the doorstep so you can get anywhere else in Hong Kong with ease. Harbourside locations seem sterile by comparison. The hotel itself rates four and a half stars --- the missing half star is the relatively small size of the rooms. But it was very quiet at nights and the air-conditioning was effective. Staff were excellent. A highlight is the rooftop swimming pool and luxurious changing rooms. Don't bother with paying for the hotel breakfast -- there is a Delifrance in the shopping centre next door at a quarter the price. One or two tips. Buy an octopus card at any MTR station (there's one immediately by the hotel) to make it particularly easy to travel around on everything from trains and trams to minibuses and the Star Ferry. Because public transport is so good there is no need for organised excursions --- much more exciting to do it yourself. We recommend Lamma Island (easy ferry ride) for an exhilarating walk between the two main villages. Stanley Market may be touristy, but it does have some great bargains. Aberdeen's high-rise developments have to be seen to be believed and take a sampan trip round its harbour (ignoring the tourist trap floating restaurants). The number 15 bus (which leaves from outside the Star Ferry terminal) is just as spectacular a method of getting up the Peak as the funicular (which often has lengthy queues). If you are there on a Sunday go to Kowloon City Park or Victoria Park for local colour.Do get out into the New Territories, especially to see the walled villages. We found Macau (70 minutes by ferry) very disappointing compared to Hong Kong.  
<Date>Apr 18, 2007

<Author>MarkK_Hanau
<Content>Very good hotel - if you want to stay in "Chinese Hong Kong" We, a group of three travellers, stayed in a Suite in the Langham Place Hotel for a week and overall, we had a fantastic experience. The hotel itself is a true 5-star hotel which offers all amenities you would expect from a hotel of such a standard. It is true, that the size of the ROOMS is a bit on the small side, but with respect to the scarcity of space in Hong Kong, this is what we expected. Rooms in upper floors over great views of the city and the harbour, even though only very few rooms seem to have an unobstructed view onto Hong Kong Island.The SERVICE was perfect - all hotel staff went out of their way to make our stay as convenient as possible. What is more, we had a few additional wishes which we voiced prior to our arrival - and everything was settled perfectly when we arrived. I know, this should be the norm, but I also know it isn't...If you can afford it, book a room that grants access to the EXECUTIVE LOUNGE, as the service there was the best I have experienced in such a facility, with free drinks throughout the day and differing (and tasty) snacks that varied according to the daytime. There is also free Internet access on three (a bit slow) computers in a designated area that offers a certain amount of privacy.BREAKFAST is plentiful and offers more than enough variety (English, Continental, Asian), even though those who need their breakfast light and sweet might complain that they have seen larger varieties in other 5-star-hotels.The LOCATION is very good, if you want the Chinese Hong Kong experience (which we did) as the hotel is situated in the center of the bustling Mongkok, which must be the most Chinese area of Hong Kong. The area is always overcrowded with people and a number of different markets are around the corner - very interesting! As the MTR (Hong Kong's adorable public transport system) is literally underneath the hotel, Hong Kong Island is easily accessible by train. Still, if you are looking for a more conservative, business like area, Mongkok might NOT be the place you want to stay in. The one thing the location does not offer, is a good bar (I mean the place to drink, not a restaurant - there are hundreds in the area!) around the corner, as these are somehow crammed into two neighborhoods that are not within walking distance (Hong Kong citizens seem to like their specialists all in the same place, there are streets full of butchers, smiths, florists, dog barbers etc...).All in all, we were very satisfied with the hotel and felt that it offered very good value for money as it is one of the less expensive 5-star-hotels in Hong Kong.  
<Date>Apr 11, 2007

<Content>A high tech hotel Despite a number of positive reviews here, I was a bit hesitant when I originally decided to book a room, because Mong-Kok is a very busy area and a bit far from the places I needed to go.I took a direct bus (Hotel Shuttle) to the hotel from the airport which took about 40 minutes. <Author>sak3
<Content>Let's Not Get Carried Away The positive reviews from Tripadvisor lead us to book this hotel and in general we had a similar positive experience as most people who have placed a review. But I feel a number of the reviews have lacked some balance. Having stayed at a few hotels around the world I can offer the opinion that this is definitely a four star hotel pretending to be five (as sold to us via the British Airways website). On the positive side the health spa, food and staff were all excellent and the hotel is well located for the MTR and shopping in Mongkok. The health spa and facilities are some of the best I have used.Where the hotel is let down (and this is based on an Executive Room) is the room size. The hotel has tried to fit a very large bed (super king or possibly larger) into a room which then barely leaves you space to walk around it. The entrance to the room is simialrly narrow and the bathroom whilst very well appointed (the rain fall shower is excellent) is also on the small side. I know space is at a premium in HK, but if you are going to be ranked at 5 stars then this hotel does not make the grade. Also a number of people have comment about the 42 plasma TV hung off the wall - unfortuantley this is completely out of propotion to the room size.I know it all sound like nit picking - but 5 star should leave no room for criticism.The other thing, and it is somethng which is a bit intangible is that the hotel did not leave us with that 5 star wow impression. Perhaps it was the understated entrance and reception or that things gets lost in translation when speaking to the staff.Overall a very good 4 star hotel and worth a stay - but defintely not a 5.

<Author>crumpet15
<Content>A Great Hotel Despite Challenging Location A Great Hotel Despite Challenging LocationI booked a week at the LPH after reading several TripAdvisor reviews. I stayed at LPH over the Chinese New Year Week this February with my family. For tourists willing to brave a very crowded location, this hotel is worth the effort. There is almost too much to cover -- everything at this hotel is first rate: rooms (pretty small), service, food quality, and hospitality. The hotel's reservations department was helpful with rate comparisons, room selection, and transportation options -- even assisting me in planning my itineraries within Hong Kong and China. I wish I'd known that they have a Skype service that allows you to speak direct with the HK reservations office! Finding this hotel is not too easy unless you're familiar with Hong Kong -- even though its is centrally located. If coming by in PM, I'd cab it from the airport. Upon check-in, we were upgraded to an executive room, which is the same as their regular room except on a higher floor. The rooms are small but decked out with the latest technology and the bathrooms are really plush. The rainshowers are awesome but you must remember to pull down the room shade for privacy! My only complaint is that even with all the high tech upgrades, you still have to pay for internet access in your room -- even with an ethernet cable! They do have free PCs/Macs on the 5th floor and Club level.  We sprang for the Club Level service, which was an expensive addition to our bargain rate, but well worth the price, as it included breakfast, snacks/beverages throughout the day. The best feature through was having a large and comfortable place to sit and hang out -- with computer access, TVs, a massage chair-- the works! And the staff there couldn't be nicer! Uncrowded space is at a premium in HK, so this was a real treat. The hotel even opened a private meeting room that had a great view of Victoria Harbor for Club guests to watch the New Year fireworks!The food at all the hotel's restaurants is great, but I thought the best value was at their upscale Ming Court restaurant on the 6th Floor. My 7 year old son particularly liked the chocolate fountains and awesome dessert buffet at The Place. Also, there are about 100 restaurants next door at the Langham Mall! The Chuan Spa is also fantastic -- access to the pool, gym, lounge, and steam/sauna are complimentary, and there is a meditation area for guests to hang out in if you don't go for the Club level. The only drawback of the hotel is its rather overcrowded location in Mong Kok. There are throngs of people everywhere -- but it also puts you within easy access by MTR to everywhere in HK. Overall a great hotel and wonderful experience.

<Author>sbendernd
<Content>Mixed Experience I spent the final two (2) days of February '07 at Langham Place. My experience, for the most part, was mixed at best. In other words, some things they seemed to do very well, while regrettably totally missing the mark on others.From a logistics standpoint, getting to the hotel from the airport was relatively straightforward as Langham had a desk just outside the baggage claim area (ie. - In fact there were a bunch of desks for various hotels there!) enabling one to take a chartered bus directly to the property for 130 H.K. dollars one way or approximately $34.00 and change U.S. currency, round trip. Alternatively a fancy private car to the property would've cost 500 H.K. dollars (or $65 U.S.) one way, but was hardly worth the extra money as the bus was quite comfortable and uncrowded, with the trip itself taking approximately 40 minutes.Also, contrary to information from my Hong Kong born and raised co-worker, who advised that the quickest way to Langham Place was by taking the Airport Express (train) to the Kowloon station and hailing a cab from there (ie. - perhaps this would've been a bit cheaper and faster alternative). But the bus, again, was fine. And my co-worker's other horror stories about midday street traffic tie-ups in Hong Kong never materialized either, as traffic was surprisingly free flowing in fact (ie. - Perhaps if I'd arrived during commute hours this wouldn't have been the case; but I can't say).Otherwise, at the hotel itself, service was quite good, in certain respects, as there were always attendants on hand to hail me taxis (ie. - almost NO wait time for taxis, in fact, as they always seemed to be queued up just beyond the hotel's main driveway at all times) and answer questions about walking directions or other activities / sites available for exploration in the immediate area (ie. - Also, as a sidelight, it's worth mentioning that the hotel's main lobby area was two elevator levels above the street level, where taxis and other hotel employees were posted. The hotel was also adjacent to a bustling shopping mall which provided additional challenges in negotiating from the subway train stop - also in the lower levels or recesses of the mall - back to the main lobby).That aside, however, on the flip side, the nature of my interaction orginating from individuals both at the front desk and concierge station appeared rehearsed or scripted and unquestionably very rushed - albiet efficient! - if nothing else. True, they smiled on cue. But there appeared to be lacking a true sense of genuineness or sincerity behind said smiles. Case in point, I went to the concierge for instructions on how to get to Victoria Peak. But everything he told me was so hurried and involved so many points of public transit transfer that I came away feeling more daunted and confused than I did beforehand. When I secondarily asked where to view the laser light show, his responses were no more satisfactory. Essentially, no more information was ever volunteered outside of the specific boundaries of my queries posed - which hearkened back to the whole efficiency, sans (or minus) true concern for guests aura that they convey. It was really transparent to see that he (ie. - the concierge) had gone through this spiel so many times that he was just quickly spouting off all of his standard, rote responses - which is never a good thing.Never ONCE did he mention any tours - Victoria Peak, harbor night cruises to view the laser lights, or otherwise - as potential options for me to consider, which I viewed as pretty inexcusable, actually. But again, you only appeared to get what you asked for and anything beyond that must have evidently been outside of their training scope - which left me feeling somewhat cold and unimpressed in general. As another sidelight, though, I was determined not to be outdone by the initial perfunctory responses received from the concierge, so I revisited him on at least a couple of other occasions - that very same day! - and peppered him with enough questions to finally get him to break out of his facade mode and loosen up to a point wherein I was actually able to extract some useful information from him at long last! Regarding food service, I had decided to take advantage of the breakfast option offered as an addition to the regular room rate. However, dining room service proved to be lacking somewhat, as I had to continually wave at various servers (ie. - and there were many!) floating around the room, to get water refills, for instance. However, the food itself was excellent, featuring both standard American fare as well as Chinese Dim Sum / noodles and other breakfast / luncheon delicacies. The deluxe room I had was a bit on the smaller side (ie. - Perhaps this is common for Hong Kong? But it certainly paled in comparison to the huge rooms in Thailand I'd just stayed in preceding my Hong Kong visit, for lesser cost). Also, I was very disappointed by the level of information provided about all of the various high tech gadgetry in the room (ie. - which would've required a separate orientation session by itself!), as the bellman didn't inform that the power in the room would be disabled if the door's key card wasn't properly placed in the slot just adjacent to the door inside. There was also the electronic touch pad temperature control panel which wasn't explained, nor the button you must push signifying whether you either: 1.) wanted the room cleaned or alternatively wanted the, 2) do not disturb message enabled. Nobody elucidated any of this in advance. The see through glass wall from bedroom to bathroom was acceptable, as I was alone. However, if I'd traveled with a significant other this may (or may not) have been an issue. Furthermore, I had significant problems with the television set, as when I was turning off all of the various light switches in the room - to retire for the evening - one of the switches somehow temporarily shorted out the t.v. - to my dismay. As it was too late to call up anybody, however, I decided to tough it out until the following day. It was at that time that I was only able to get the t.v. up and running again by experimenting with the door key card. Specifically, I removed it from the slot - intentionally turning off all power in the room altogether - and re-inserted it back in the slot (ie. - sort of emulating a trip switch). Upon doing so, the t.v. powered back on. However, afterwards, the t.v.'s pictures kept freezing up periodically, which was also a major annoyance.And oh yes, lest I forget, to add final insult to injury no one informed that the elevators wouldn't work between 11 p.m. and 7 a.m. unless you inserted your door key cards in a little slot in the elevator. So the scenario was this. Specifically, it's after 11 p.m. Me and another couple - whom I didn't know - entered the elevator and the door closed behind us as usual. However, when we punched the buttons for our respective floors, nothing happened, and after a few seconds the elevator door opened on its own, having never moved from our floor of entry, at all. After a confused minute or two, way off down in the lower left hand corner of the elevator - in small print - we finally noticed a little placard and card slot instructing us that the elevators wouldn't work between said hours unless we inserted the door cards, into the slot accordingly. Again, wasn't it real nice of Langham Place to share that little tidbit of knowledge with us in advance (ie. - sic)?!On a positive note, however, without any great hassle nor fanfare, whatsoever, the hotel did allow me one extra hour until checkout for greater compatibility with my flight schedule, which was appreciated.Through it all, I'd probably stay at Langham Place again, on a subsequent visit to Hong Kong. I'd probably try upgrading the room, however. But in either event, I'd certainly perform more due diligence in checking around for other alternatives next time, rather than simply accepting all of the glowing reviews I'd read in Trip Advisor as unassailable or the end all gospel word. Because the property still has a road long traveled ahead of itself to achieve true 4 or 5 star status in my humble estimation.

<Author>highfly
<Content>Really different and quirky We spent 3 nights here and booked a club room which gave access to a lovely lounge with food and drinks, internet access, fab views and a massage chair.The bedroom also had magnificent views over the city and was well equipped with huge flat screen tv, and dvds available to borrow from a library. Toiletries were lovely and there was everything you could need. Breakfast was in the club lounge but you had the free option of buffett breakfast downstairs ( I think they probably had to do this as lounge could get busy) The location is very different as the hotel and attched shopping centre are part of a big development investment in Mongkok - which is a real local area and not the traditional touristy part. The streets outside are brilliant to walk around - a real hive of activity with people making everything in front of you - from rivets to coffins and shoes to bathroom fittings. It is really atmospheric yet so easy to get to the sights by subway which is the best subway I have used anywhere in the world.On arriving at the hotel a girl with shocking pink gloves and a funny hat calls the lift for you! Its little things which are quirky/nice!Only downside ( and its not a huge thing) was that we queued to check in only to be told that we should have gone straight to the club floor to check in. When we got there we had to queue again. The club checkin frequently had people waiting so maybe that is a process which could be improved.All in all a fantastic place which I would recommend. Thanks to Trip Advisor as it was through the recommendations there that I booked it.

<Content>Absolutely a great place to stay My wife and I stayed here for four days in February and both of us absolutly loved it. <Author>ozzyvirgin
<Content>Fantastic Hotel This was our first visit to Hong Kong, a 3 night stopover on our way to Australia. After much deliberation (should we book harbour view hotel / shouldn't we book harbour view hotel) we decided on a non harbour view hotel to fit in with our budget. We decided on the Langham Place Hotel in Mongkok. Before arriving, we were unsure of the area/location of hotel and the style of hotel. We were not at all disappointed. As soon as you arrive at the hotel you will be impressed. We checked in and went straight to the bar which happened to have happy hour at the time. Great food and drink menu selection with seafood counter. Buzzy yet at the same time relaxing environment. The hotel location is fabulous. Right on top of an MTR station with easy connections to travel all over the city. A very easy underground system to use with safe, clean, fast, regular trains. Easy to get anywhere on Kowloon or the Island. The hotel is within very easy walking distance to the famous markets and shopping streets. Speak to concierge (who are excellent and can help with all queries, questions and directions). Regarding the hotel, we had a standard room on 27th floor which we were very pleased with. Very comfortable, great bed and bathroom (with glass walls!!). Good views too. Hotel is attached to large shopping complex (access via reception) which is great for shopping but also has a food hall with menus to suit all. Even if you don't manage a swim, be sure to take a look at the hotel rooftop pool. Enjoy! We would definitely stay at this hotel again.

<Author>BJMCNAUGHT
<Content>Proof of the Pudding Stayed here for three nights as the first leg of a trip which then went on to Thailand. The hotel itself is impressive. Good rooms, lovely spa, great bar serving very good food and wine and some of that dodgy entertainment in hotels that you only get in HK and Dubai and such like. The issue with this hotel is the location which is in Mongkok, not HK island itself. Mongkok is a very busy residential area with lots of markets. If you are willing to take taxis and get the underground as we were, it is good as a value for money option. The hotel is in a shopping mall so if you're feeling tired and it's too hot to go outside, that is an option. The tube station is in the shopping mall so it's not far to get to the harbour area or onto HK island itself. If I were to return to HK, I wouldn't automatically book into this hotel which is maybe proof of the pudding that it wasn't 'all that'.

<Author>A2DL
<Content>Loved Langham Place My sister and I traveled to Hong Kong for a cultural experience we will never forget. After reading the ranking on TripAdvisor I decided to book our 9 night stay at the Langham Place Hotel. It was fantastic! There were a few things that were particularly nice: (1) the hotel bar/lounge scene which had great food and drinks which we enjoyed immensely before heading out on the town on our 1st night and many more to follow (2) the cleanliness (3) the location - Mongkok gives one more of a 'local' feel of Hong Kong (4) while on the small side, the beds and pillows were great as was the rain shower, especially after the long flight (5) the fitness facility, we saved our HK$ and skipped the spa but loved the free sauna  gym (6) the hotel staff - unfortunately I came down with bronchitis (too many nights at the bar I suppose) and the front desk arranged for a doctor to come to my room the following morning. For only HK$1500 I received excellent medical care which included all of the prescription drugs. Honestly the only thing I would like to change would be the slow lifts/elevators. Buy an octopus card and travel on the MTR like a pro. It's incredibly easy to get all around HK and much faster than taking a taxi.

<Content>Fantastic hotel, fantastic location! I read so much about this hotel before taking the plunge and booking it. Well the first bad experience was to catch the underground to Mong-Kok (hotel location) with a cranky wife, 2 hungry 3 year old boys  about 60kg of luggage. The underground is about a 6 escalator trips + short walks to the hotel lobby and it does not stick out in your face even when your at the lobby level because you are actually in a shopping mall. Reception were very receptive and offered me a couple of clean nicely rolled face washers to wipe my face down. I was given a room on the 29th floor  unfortunately it was really musky smelling like the carpet had been wet for a while and not dried properly. I thought it would eventually go but it didn't so I called them to which they were happy to move me to another room.That was the last of the negative things about the hotel  location. For the next 5 days we had the time of our lives with the great room, fine view, 42 plasma, DVD, unreal bathroom, comfortable bed, etc..and my personal favourite - The Location. The hotel sits above a shopping mall/eatery as well having markets  shops galore in the surrounding area. We were going out shopping at 10pm for a couple of hours then having a bite to eat before going to bed at around 1-2am (we had a friend babysitting). For good coffee try the place next to the long escalator in the Langham mall. The eatery in the mall also offers good value food as well. We are planning to be back again in 2007 and hopefully we will can appreaciate just as much next time.

<Author>Ridgesas
<Content>Great Hotel and Service, Good Location Stayed here for 5 nights in Nov/Dec. Used the hotel shuttle from the airport as we had 4 large bags and did not want to use the Express Train and handle the baggage. Room was smaller than expected but did have a great bed with a choice of pillows, great amenities and a wonderful view of Hong Kong. The washroom with glass walls takes a little getting used to but makes the room feel bigger and more contemporary.The service was great. About 3 days after checking in I went down to request another key. I spoke to the same agent who had checked me in and she remembered my name and the room number!On one night I wondered down to the buffet resteraunt to purchase a few crackers as I had an upset stomach. I was immediately given some crackers from the buffet and told not to worry when I offered to pay.As other reviews have stated, the pool and gym area are well maintained, very modern and offer great views of Hong Kong.I really liked the location. Mong Kok is only 2 MTR stops from Kowloon and a good base for any visitor. Wonderful shopping and resteraunts all around. When we were walking around Kowloon we were constantly being bothered with offers for suits etc. You will not find this in Mong Kok as I feel this is where many of the locals eat and shop (vs. the tourists). Make sure to try the Dim Sum resteraunt (on level 3) located in the mall next to the hotel. Some of the best Dim Sum I have ever tried!
