<Author>hxdirect
<Content>Wow!! We booked this hotel because our first choice, based on this website, Hotel Nikko was unavailable. Having stayed in the Langham Place I'm glad.Langham Place is in the bustling area of Mongkok. The hotel is attached to a shopping centre which has a food court with an immense variety of food outlets. It is also surrounded by streets full of shops and markets which have an unbelievable atmosphere both during the day and at night.The hotel itself wholeheartedly deserves it's 5* rating. The quality, efficiency and warmth of the staff, from the moment you step out of the taxi is wonderfull. Little touches such as the beautiful scent which greets you when you walk in, to the refreshing towels the staff give you whilst you are checking in make the experience, for someone who doesn't normally book 5* unless the rate is too good to miss.The room we booked was an executive room and we were more than happy with the standard of comfort and cleanliness. The bed was huge and we were offerred a choice of differently scented pillows. Having already read the reviews on the TA website we were well aware that the wall between the ensuite and the main bedroom was made of glass and we found this added to the feeling of space in the room. Besides that if you wanted you could watch the Plasma TV from the bath if you wanted.It was quite hot in Hong Kong when we were there which we were not expecting and so we found that upon returning to the hotel after a long days sightseeing and shopping we needed to refresh and shower. The main thing which impressed us was that when the staff came to turn down the bed in the evening they also completely cleaned and replenished the bathroom and shower area again rather than wait until the next morning.We eat breakfast in the hotel on a couple of mornings and the choice was wide ranging and excellent. I particularly liked the fact that the honey was from a honeycomb. We also spent most evenings in the bar which had an excellent Canadian jazz singer on most nights. The atmosphere was congenial, the choice of drinks good and should you get hungry they had an excellent display of fresh seafood (oysters etc) for you to choose from.All in all I would have to say this hotel has it all. I worried initially that it's location away from the harbour would be inconvenient but the MTR was right on the doorstep and the surrounding streets were lively and vibrant. We will definitely be back.

<Author>NickfromLondon
<Content>Langham Place is THE Place to Stay in Hong Kong First Class Five Star Hotel with terrific contemporary design which manages to avoid the stuffiness of competing Five Star Hotels in HK. Situated in real Hong Kong with hustle and bustle of local Chinese in the surrounding streets. Avoids the rather sterile Central Business District atmosphere of eg Four Seasons and Mandarin Oriental.Excellent communications as situated on top of Mongkok MTR giving direct access to Kow;oon waterfront and to Central. Rapid road access to Central on HK island in just ten minutes via Western Tunnel which avoids congestion around middle Harbour Tunnel.Five star service amongst the best I have seen. Unbelievable comfortable beds. Room size absoloutley fine although perhaps not as big as at some five star establishments - but bigger than I expected having seen some comments on this website. Excellent bathrooms with glazed screen providing breathtaking views.Relaxed and buzzing Portal bar full of wealthy Hong Kong Chinese as well as hotel guests. Terrific live Jazz every evening (except Sunday).A great hotel for a businessman wanting to escape from the sterile atmosphere surrounding Mandarin Oriental or Four Seasons and great for wealthier tourists too. Can't receommend it highly enough - I will be back.

<Author>mirey
<Content>Best Hotel Yet We arrived in Hong Kong after a 3 week tour of mainland China following the Silk Road so this hotel was an oasis that allowed us to recuperate before returning home. The rooms were spacious enough (despite what some of the other reviewers have said); the beds were unbelievably comfortable; the see-through wall between the bathroom and the bedroom was a bit disconcerting at first until you realized that you could have a view of Hong Kong at night from the luxurious bath; separate rain shower; everything immaculately clean; quiet despite being located in the bustling heart of street markets in Kowloon; free computer usage at the Portal 24/7. Of the many bests about this hotel, one was the fantastic and varied buffet breakfast delivering anything from poached eggs made by the omelet chef for you (a rarity at a hotel), fresh honey from a honeycomb, home made jams, breads of every variety including gluten free, a chocolate fountain in which you could dunk donuts (kids would love this) -- you get the picture. Another was the well-equipped gym and beautiful rooftop pool located in the Spa area. Try this at night when there are few guests and the ceiling is open to the night air. We didn't try the spa itself but the change rooms, including plunge pool and sauna and wonderful showers, as well as every possible amenity for washing and drying your hair, were quite spectacular.Lastly, the service was excellent, from the front desk clerk to the restaurant staff, from the maids to the spa staff, from the concierge desk to the lovely ladies in pink suits opening doors for you. During our stay, we were fortunate enough to be invited to a manager's cocktail party in a lovely outdoor space behind the breakfast restaurant -- the Backyard. There we got to meet some of the hotel management who made the Langham Place work as seamlessly as it does.We were so happy that we decided to stay in Kowloon. Access to all of Hong Kong's tourist areas was a short and comfortable MTR ride away. Some reviewers complained about the walk to the subway station but either through the Mall or from the outside, it was a short hike. We were lucky enough to encounter a clear morning on Victoria Peak and so got a good view of this lovely City. In the evenings, we trolled the street markets and enjoyed the bargains, especially on the electronics street practically adjacent to the hotel.The shopping mall, attached by a walkway to the hotel, had a variety of restaurants, a Starbucks if you're missing that cappuccino. We particularly enjoyed Genki Sushi, a fast food sushi bar where the sushi plates are delivered to you via conveyer belt and the bill is calculated by totting up the various coloured plates left over.We have stayed at many hotels around the world and the Langham Place is our favourite so far.  
<Date>Nov 7, 2006

<Content>Loved it We stayed for six nights in late October. The hotel was great. Rooms, service  food were fantastic. <Author>mschneider
<Content>Excellent Breakfast Stayed for three nights in the standard rooms. Even though this was a brand new hotel, I thought the decor of the room, especially the bathroom to be quite ugly! Room was small but functional. Air contditionaing was fantastic with an easy to use digital thermostat. A power adapter and ethernet cable is provided free of charge inside the mini-bar. Broadband internet (both wired  wifi) was super-fast but not free. The business center/bar provies about ten terminals to suft the web free of chrage(20 minute time limit). A poster below found the rooms to be noisy and the elevators slow-that was not my experience. No noise from the street or from the hallway, and no problems with the elevators. But I agree that getting to the hotel from the subway station via the mall was frustrating; you have to go up five different escalators. I quickly learned that exiting the station via portland st. and walking around the exterior of the mall to the hotel was much quicker. I had no problems with the location; hotel is just a five minute walk from the northen tip of the temple street night market, and everything else is just quick train ride away with Hong Kong's super efficient subway system.But the highlight of this hotel was the incredible buffet breakfast! Fresh honey from a honeycomb, fresh queezed OJ, and place mats with current news headlines and weather. If the price is right, I wouldn't hesitate to stay again. P.S. If you don't do the hiking trail around the peak, you should have your passport revoked :)

<Author>StuartCraig
<Content>Top quality hotel with bags of style The Langham Place sets out it's stall as one of the top hotels in the world and certainly pulls it off. We stayed for a few nights en route to Australia and being familiar with most of the top hotels in Hong Kong, we were blown away by this place!It's a hi-tech paradise with IP phones, plasma screens and DVD players - complete with free movies - but you shouldn't overlook the fantastic spa and roof-top swimming pool. Most evenings we had this all to ourselves and felt like kings. A Mongkok location is not the most central but getting around HK is always straightforward and Mongkok is certainly a vibrant place. The adjoining Langham Place Mall is enormous and is like walking through the set of Blade Runner! Food options are plentiful with some excellent restaurants on the top floor of the mall. Surpisingly though, hotel restaurants were good value and the Ming Court in particular is top quality.We took our 10 year old son to this hotel and he was treated very well by all the pleasant staff and our experience was certainly made all the better by the courtesy of everybody who works at the Langham Place.

<Author>simonrip
<Content>Really Quite Overrated I booked this hotel for a short business trip based on the numerous glowing reports from this site. I should make clear that I have been fortunate to stay in some of the finest hotels, but I am equally happy in medium-class hotels if they offer more than the price would lead you to expect. I appreciate that, by HK standards, this is not a particularly expensive hotel, but it really was quite disappointing. There were no huge flaws, just a number of small annoyances which added up to a rather unsatisfactory experience. The most important problem for me was noise. In a hotel of this class, especially a new hotel, you don't expect to be able to hear the TV in the room next door, or the occupants coughing  talking. This is a pet hate of mine, and is just not acceptable. The other guests were also very noisy, and I was woken up on Friday  Saturday nights after 1am by guests returning to their rooms, laughing  talking loudly in the corridors. I know the hotel can't really be held responsbile for this, but that is the kind of clientele it attracts.Next complaint, the location is certainly not ideal. For those who don't know HK, Mongkok is really a bit far out from the action - certainly for tourists. I did know this, but read that the MTR (subway) station was close, and so wasn't concerned. However, whilst the entrance to the MTR is in the shopping mall attached to the hotel, you have to walk right through the mall and down several levels to reach it. This is a good 10-15 minute walk, and so not as handy as you expect. If you want to walk to Tsim Sha Tsui (the part of Kowloon adjacent to HK island, where the 'tourist' area is), you will be walking for more than an hour.The lifts: You will think I am mad, but this hotel has the slowest lifts ever. On accasion, I was waiting for over 5 minutes for a lift to arrive, which is infuriating if you are as impatient as me. I guess there are simply not enough lifts to service the rooms effectively.On the plus side, the rooms are well equipped, with large plasma TVs, and sumptuous bathrooms - the huge rain showers are nearly powerful enough to knock you over. The bed is one of the most comfortable I have ever slept in, and they offer a wide range of pillows to ensure you have something to cover up the sound of the other guest arriving back (or just to sleep on perhaps).The Spa is impressive, and they do offer a very nice massage to ease away the aches of the long flight. However, the pool tends to be surrounded by Spa guests on loungers, so you may feel uncomfortable using it if you are a bit self-conscious. The service is also quite good, but I have never found poor service yet in any hotel in this part of the world.I am sure those with different expectations to mine would be happy here, but I recommend you pick a good hotel closer to, or on, the island instead.Simon  
<Date>Oct 19, 2006

<Author>vktang
<Content>Fabulous hotel! The hotel is the newer, more beautiful sister to the Langham Hotel in Tsim Sha Tsui, and it is connected to a huge mall in Kowloon. While the Tsim Sha Tsui location is more desirable (with top brand name shopping like Gucci, Hermes, Ferragamo, etc) just a stone's throw from the hotel, I liked the Mongkok location better (I have stayed at both) because of the convenience factor. You can get to the metro without ever leaving the building, since it is connected to the mall. There is also an impressive food court in the mall. As for the hotel itself, our room was gorgeous, and there is a pillow menu from which you can choose a scented pillow (even though the regular pillows are great too). The only oddity about the room was that the wall between the bathroom and the bedroom area was made of clear glass (presumably so that you can watch TV while you take a bath), but it really freaked me out. Don't worry, though. There is a shade that you can pull down.The gym and spa are located on a very high floor, so there is a great view of the city and harbor as you are exercising. The spa is expensive (what I would consider top end New York City prices).The service was incredible. Everyone was extremely helpful at the hotel. I would not hesitate to stay there again.

<Author>wenrobbo
<Content>Had a wonderful time We stayed for four nights at the end of July and absolutely loved the experience. We arrived about 11am but no problems checking in then. Fantastic view from our room on the 29th floor. We requested and got a non smoking room. touches I really liked - ice making machine on each floor, huge plasma tv with free dvd hire, free internet access from the business centre, friendly staff, great roof top pool - and his and hers showers, steam room and sauna. In fact, when we said we had a late night flight, they let us check out at 1pm but suggested using these facilities and the locker room. This meant we had a relaxing time by the pool, a great shower, changed into fresh clothes before going. Yes, the room wasn't gigantic - but the views from the window and the glass wall between the bedroom and bathroom made it seem more spacious. And there is a blind you can pull down for privacy! I loved where it was located. Great shopping mall for the food court and the more up market retaurants on the higher floors. We had many meals at both. Close to the MTR, and close to some great local markets. Warning - tonic water is very difficult to find. I found one place nearby only. And my husband wanted tomato juice, which on the suggestion of the staff we got in the shopping plaza with international food where the big ships come in. I would definitely stay here again.

<Author>Smiley2!
<Content>We felt like Royalty!! I just cannot believe that anyone would have anything negative to say about this hotel as it is just beautiful and a true 5*! The staff go out of their way to please you and everywhere you walk, staff smile and wish you 'Good Morning' Even the 'Breakfast staff' in The Place remembered each morning as to whether we preffered tea or coffee and graciously poured it out for us as soon as we sat down to have our breakfast. The Hotel is stunning and immaculate - I am very fussy and I could not fault anything!I have just returned from spending 10 days there with my Husband and 2 children. We stayed in the Kowloon Quad Room and had an excellent deal which included breakfast (Which is amazing - and complete with fruit and chocolate fountains!) The room was spacious and it was a pleasant change that my children did not have to sleep on a Z-Bed but in a 'Blissful' bed of their own! Do not take any toiletries - the hotel provides every single item you will need for your stay - there is also a complimentary umbrella for you to use during your stay. I will not repeat what others have written as readers can scroll down and read about the plasma TV, views, Spa etc but I will just say that all of the mentioned by others exceeded our expectations making if so hard to leave at the end of our stay! Location wise - Mongkok is very exciting! My children are ages 10 and 11 years and did not get bothered by the crowds, but enjoyed watching everyone and looking into restaurants and seeing the hustle and bustle of 'Real' life. We would not stay anywhere else as we had the best of both worlds. We could easily get up to New Territories or down to Central. We liked the location of Mongkok instead of the clinical world of designer shops and high prices. After the 3rd shopping centre, we were bored with the designer shops and shopped in Mongkok where we shopped with the locals which was much more stimulating! (And did not have tourist prices or any tailors nagging you for business everywhere you walked!)Tourist sights - All the usual ones are fantastic but we had our best experiences were with heritage classes, such as Cantonese Opera and Feng Shui classes with the Hong Kong Tourist Board.We cannot wait to stay at Langham Place again and if you are toying with the idea of staying here, I urge you to try this fabulous hotel! You will LOVE it! The Hotel does 'Early Bird Saver Rate' if you book a few months in advance including breakfast!

<Author>kizzypoo2
<Content>Bad Service, Terrible Decor, and a Mold Problem Have you ever had a friend that has spent a lot of money on an outfit, and the end result is that she/he still appears tacky or tawdry? Well that describes the Langham Place Hotel in Hong Kong to a tee. During our second visit to Hong Kong, we were very enthusiastic about staying at the Langham Place after reading many good reviews. Unfortunately our experience did not live up to our high expectations. The Langham is far from a 5-star hotel. We arrived after a late flight and the first room we were given was small and cramped, the d茅cor was gaudy and worse, it had a serious mold problem. The mold was particularly challenging since my mother has severe allergies and is asthmatic. Because of her health condition we had to switch rooms, but when we asked to be moved to another room we were told there were no other rooms available except for a smoking room or one where we had to upgrade to one of their packages which included brunch, tea, and drinks (none of which we needed because we had many tours scheduled and didn鈥檛 need to eat at the hotel). We were told that this would be the only way we could change rooms, and since the smoking room was out of the question and it was so late at night, we had no choice but to acquiesce. What they neglected to tell us was that we were being moved to a room that was the exact same size (far smaller than the advertised 300+ square feet). The room was uncomfortable - very cluttered with art, glass accents, and an enormous bed that took up most of the room. We were very disappointed by the whole experience. After just one night, we cancelled our reservation and switched hotels (we spent the remainder of our trip comfortably at the less glossy but more tasteful JW Marriott). Though we believe the lobby, bar, and dining area at the Langham Place to be lovely, the two Executive Rooms we encountered were dismal, and we simply did not appreciate having to pay more money for a room that was the same size, and a dining package we never used. Honestly we would have preferred a comfortable room over a room stuffed full of low-end high-tech gadgets. Based on our room, we couldn鈥檛 imagine that this hotel was the very same that had received such glowing reviews! If you are a traveler that spends a great deal of time in hotel bars, lounges and restaurants, and less time in your room, perhaps the Langham Place would be good fit. But if you desire a hotel with a full package, this is not the hotel for you. Overall, I would not recommend Langham Place.

<Author>Love_flying
<Content>An oasis of calm, style and excellent service! I stayed at the Langham Place for 7 nights from June 18th and had a fantastic holiday. Upon arrival the staff were courteous, efficient and welcoming - I stayed with 2 friends and we had booked a triple room but were upgraded to a much larger quad room without having to ask. The hotel is immaculate, the whole hotel has a light fragrance of jasmine - not overpowering but pleasant and the views over Hong Kong island are among the best I have ever experienced.Our room was on the 26th floor and was perfect. The widescreen plasma TV was a real plus as were the speakers in the bathroom enabling you to watch TV or listen to the radio in the bath (assuming nobody else was in the room as the wall of the bathroom is glass with a blind that you can pull down!). The shower was among the most spacious I have seen in hotels with a huge central shower head - the 'rain effect' shower - and a seperate portable shower head. It was an absolute delight! The housekeeping service was flawless and our beds were turned down in the early evening whilst we were out and slippers placed by our bed along with a complimentary bottle of water.The breakfast at 'the place' restaurant was a fantastic buffet mix of Western and Chinese breakfast options, ranging from pancakes to dim sum and was extremely good value for money. The bar was stylish and had jazz performances in the evenings and some delicious cocktails on the menu (I especially liked the Sake lady!). Next to the bar was a work area with free access to the internet from a selection of PCs and Macs; I found this especially useful for emailing friends/colleagues and for reconfirming and online check in for my flights.For me the highlight of the hotel is the Chuan Spa on the 41st floor. The changing rooms are in themselves well designed and every possible need catered for with a sauna, steam room and jaccuzi (which is next to a window overlooking the city in the men's - so relaxing!) as well as provision of all toiletries one could ever need. The pool area was, contrary to the previous review, open throughout my stay and I made use of it both at night and during the day, affording a supremely relaxing experience and an unrivalled view from the open air pool!The langham mall adjacent to the hotel has Starbucks and many other small cafes that we used on days when we felt a lighter breakfast or just an iced coffee was necessary! The MTR (subway/underground) has a station right outside the hotel and is extremely convenient for accessing Kowloon and Hong Kong itself. We felt the location was actually preferable to central HK as the surrounds felt far more authentic and offered a better experience of Hong Kong life.Overall I would highly recommend this hotel - it is certainly the best value 5* (it truely IS a 5* hotel, contrary to other reviews!) hotel I have ever stayed at and I look forward to the day I can go back to Hong Kong as I most certainly will be staying here!

<Author>Babyboomer2
<Content>Breathtaking design statement Just returned from a wonderful time at the Langham Place and can't rave enough about it. It was a bold decision to build a very modern, design statement hotel in a non-tourist type environment-but it works! Everything about the hotel spells attention to detail, from the edgy floral arrangements to the wonderful smell of ginger flowers that wafted throughout the public areas ( I bought bottles of the stuff to take home as presents!) The lounge/bar area is jazz cool and if you want to shop upscale or grab a Starbucks there is a multistory, brand new shopping mall attached. Or if you'd rather eat with the locals and shop at the markets, just step outside the front door( Ladies Market is just around the corner). The rooms are Hong Kong small, but very comfortable with plasma screen TV on the wall and a huge rain shower and glass sink in the bathroom. We had three people in our room(husband , son and I ) with one queen and two twin beds and still plenty of room for luggage etc so while small-good utilization of space. This isnt the hotel to stay in if your looking for harbour views but we had a breathtaking view of the city and loved the neon frenzy just outside of the hotel. Mongkok station is attached to the Langham Shopping Mall if you want to use Hong Kong's great public transport system or avail yourself of the inexpensive taxis from the lobby entrance to the hotel. We really enjoyed our time at this hotel and would have no hesitation about recommending it to others.

<Author>Jane0870
<Content>Wonderful hotel! We stayed at the Langham Place Hotel for 3 nights in April, 2006. It was a divine experience. We were a traveling trio of grandmother, mother and daughter. Upon arrival we were pleased to find 3 twin beds instead of the typical double beds which require sharing. The beds were very comfortable, unlike many of the very hard beds you usually find in Hong Kong. The view from our 32nd floor room was spectacular. We highly recommend the lunch buffet in the dining room. The price is very reasonable, and the selection is amazing! Dozens of entrees and salads, and a full seafood bar. The dessert island includes a chocolate fountain. I didn't expect the chocolate to be very good, but it really was superb tasting chocolate. We also enjoyed the cocktail lounge balcony in the evening. The live entertainment was excellent. The singer was very beautiful, and she had an extraordinary voice.There was a lovely fragrance wafting throughout the hotel. It was light floral and refreshing.The swimming pool and sauna were very nice.All of the wait staff personnel were helpful, gracious, and prompt. The service was definitely A+.My one and only complaint is that the packets of coffee grounds were not free in the rooms. Tea bags and powdered coffee packets were, but if you wanted to make a fresh pot you had to pay an unreasonable price. I thought this was petty, and it irritated me as I have stayed in many inexpensive hotels in the US that have free coffee pot type coffee.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Very Good Hotel We stayed at the Langham Place from the 1st to 7th March 2006 and have read lots of the reviews before going and some since my return and offer our impression.Whilst there are lots, the majority of the reviews, are favourable reviews and one recent one here not so favourable, I have to say on balance it was a nice place to stay. I do agree with one of the comments from the previous reviewer and that is the blissful bed. I have not travelled in this region before, but the bed's did seem hard and so different to what we are used to we found them difficult to get a good nights sleep in. At home we have 2000 spring bed of medium firm, and that's blissful! So as I say, this may be the norm for Chinese folk to sleep on much firmer beds. We thought they were too firm, but for those who like firmer beds they will be happy.Enough of the bed. Our experience of the hotel was very good. I asked for an upgrade when I arrived, no suites avalable but they put us in a larger triple room with big corner windows that looked over Mong Kok and down to HK island ( at no extra charge ), on the subject of charges, all things are relative to value paid, we booked through British Airways holidays and the six nights cost 拢345 for the both of us, so comparing money spent, the upgraded room, the view it was excellent value. We added breakfasts, 拢50 for the two of us, 拢50, again through British Airways, this turned out to be good value also as the bill each day for the breakfasts for two was HK$319, about 拢24 X 6 = 拢144. I agree with the previous writer the breakfasts were okay, and I did not think much of the Dim Sum. The breakfasts, they were catering for what you would normaly get in North American style hotels, but not quite as good. In the US they know how to do crispy bacon well, and the potatoes in the morning rather than the hash browns. We are still glad we had it though, plenty of selection. We found the instant we cleared our plates a waiter was there and it was removed. You only needed to usher any of the staff for refills and they delivered right away, and as I say at the price we paid, we have to say excellent value.Whilst on the restaurant, we only ate in it one evening and the selection was not really to our tastes. I know its sounds stupid, but our palates are obviously in tune with western Chinese tastes rather than the genuine chinese that was served in the resuarant so we gave it a miss. However the mall connected has an abundance of local restaurants and these are more in tune with western tastes, so we sampled a few of these. By the way the price difference of the hotel vs the mall eateries is about 90% cheaper than the hotel and about 40% cheaper in other restaurants outside of the mall. There is actually a Mortons restaurant down beside the Pinnisula hotel not far from the Star Ferry, that would be familiar to US visitors if they want a change from chinese food.We found the PC's available in the portel area working fine, with pencils and paper to hand. Connections were good. Don't know about the apple macs though, they didn't get used much, so they might not have been so good, but look impressive.Also at the portel you can borrow dvd's free of charge. Connected to the portel is the bar area, staff very good and don't leave dirty ashtrays on tables, replaced very quickly.Cleanliness is high. Our bathroom washed out each day and you could smell the disinfectant used in cleaning the bathroom. Beds turned down, and curtains pulled every evening. Our room didn't have one of those glass bathrooms but a solid wall one seperate to the bed room. It was a good size and the shower room was very good. Air Con didnt seem to get any warmer or colder whether it was at 18c or 26c. I would notice the difference in my house if I turned the central heating upto 26c, so I don't know, it met our needs anyway.Its pool on the top floor is superb as is the faclities that go with it like the changing rooms, showers, sauna, steam room, jacuzza, toiletries, hairdryers etc etc, all constanly with attendants and again, ensuring used towels are not lying around and cleaning the mirrors and everything else. Everytime we went to the pool it was hardly ever used, often we were the only people there. I had forgot my swimming trunks and had to buy a pair at the pool. Oh well it, could have been worse, I could have forgot my passportAll staff were very help full and the place was spotlessly clean wherever you went.A bit about the Location. Langham Place is slap bang in the middle of Mong Kok. Mong Kok, (meaning burstling corner) is certainly burstling. You step out the hotel through the mall and you are there. Or go the other way and you are right beside street markets of vegtables, fish and meat sellers, wonderful to see and experience and just mingle about taking it all in and taking photo's of the going on's. Other markets are right by you, like 5 minute walk to ladies market or Nathan Road or electronics street or sports street and of course the MTR Mong Kok station is there for easy access to TST or HK island itself. We bought a Octupus ticket from the MTR, HK$150 each (HK$300 in total), run about every where with it trains, buses, ferries, handed it back at the end and got HK$160 back. The whole area is safe and surprising clean for such a huge population and concentration of people (much cleaner say than London), like no cigarette ends or discarded paper or packaging on the roads or pavements, mainly because there are waste bins and ashtrays every few hunderd yards and the locals use them, so did we. If you are observant you will see the the equivalent of the cleansing department steam cleaning the alleyways with portable generators. Another thing was construction sites, vehicles leaving the site to go onto public roads roads having there tyres cleaned first so as not to soil the road.We are glad we stayed on the Kowloon side rather than HK island itself. Visiing HK island it was a bit going to a financial district down town ish if you know what I mean. Lots of designer shops, but you get these every where and if you are familiar with downtown financial districs, unless you are on business, are a bit soulless. Anyway the best veiws, for what HK is famous for, its skyline is best seen looking over from Kowloon and not on HK island.So in summary, the hotel is good, the location to experience the local buzz and everyday life can't be bettered, there are other hotels, but not with such a good location for everything being on your door step. For the cost of the deal through BA, it was excellent value for money, which is the final judgement and it certainly provide good value in my experience.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>As Superficial as a Hollywood Set Having stayed six nights at the Langham Place there is a huge disconnect between my impressions of this property and the praises sung by some of the comments listed by others on this site. The hotel in my estimation is all style and no substance. In fact, it reminds me of a Hollywood set. Once you go beyond the surface, it becomes apparent that the hotel is very ordinary and average in many ways and not deserving of anything more than 3 to 4 stars. 5 stars鈥mpossible!I break my impressions into the tangible qualities of the hotel and the intangible qualities related to service level. First, with the tangibles: I booked two rooms for my stay, one an executive room for my children and the other a studio room. The executive rooms are tiny even by HK standards. I鈥檝e stayed at every major Hong Kong hotel over the years and the only other hotel with smaller rooms is the Kowloon Hotel in TST. If you are traveling as a couple and are big boned westerners you are going to be bumping into things in the executive room. The smallness of the rooms also contributes to the deterioration that is evident in the bump and scratch that results from moving luggage that is inevitable due to space restrictions. There is limited storage space and tiny closets to house your clothes and I found we had to live out of our suitcases. The quality of the furnishings are all sizzle and no steak. All of the casework (cabinetry) are cheaply made, hollow core doors, the drawers are melamine interiors vs. real wood found in other hotels. Plus, the amount of drawerspace is limited. The carpeting reminds me of giraffe skin and feels like cheap office-commercial carpeting underfoot. The 鈥渂lissful鈥?bed is the biggest marketing hype ever, if you like your beds firm, it鈥檚 like sleeping on a slab. The large flat screen TV is a plus, but it鈥檚 there for the hotel鈥檚 benefit, there is no way they can shoehorn an armoire into the room so they put the flat screen on the wall to save space. The bathrooms look nice but is not all that functional and as with the room, is compact. The shower has no light so you shower in the dark, the marble is cheap looking white marble (the kind you see in mainland hotels in abundance), and the glass sink with countertop is an example of gee-wizz design that compromises on functionality. The counter is so small that I found our things constantly falling off it onto the floor. Look closer at the bath hardware and it鈥檚 already starting to tarnish, blister or rusted. Look at the tile grout and it鈥檚 discolored. This is not what you would expect for a so called 5 star property and one that is barely a year old. Water pressure is fine so no faults there. Desk amenities are minimal, a pad with one sheet of paper left to it, and dog-eared and stained hotel brochures and magazines. The common spaces in the hotel is where the owners put all the money. The lobbies, elevators and entry are all very nicely decorated using expensive finishes. The original art is also quite nice to look at. The tradeoff is a richer look in the common areas at the expense of the rooms. Restaurants and Bars 鈥?we ate the buffet breakfast at the Place. The buffet is nothing to write home about. Very ordinary by HK standards. The dim-sum selections barely edible. Service was chaotic. I observed many people running around in frenzied activity but they would pass us up ten times with dirty plates piling up on the table. I had to ask for coffee refills every time even though the coffee lady walked by us a dozen times. Kind of reminded me of an episode of the keystone cops, a lot of activity but none of it actually orchestrated in a meaningful way. I wanted to write a comment to the manager of the service in the buffet, but when I pulled out the comment card that was attached to the payment bill I found it was an older one already filled out by another customer dated several months earlier. I was astonished to find that the staff does little to read or process customer comment cards! After two breakfasts in the hotel, we decamped for the eateries in the adjoining shopping mall. Management needs to work on this. Had evening drinks upstars in the lounge. Very good house band with nice vocals by a stylish and attractive singer. Drinks service was very attentive and prices similar to other HK hotels. The lounge is not big by HK standards and overlooks the lobby.The computer area (Portal) is also not very well managed. At any given time, several PC鈥檚 not operating, broken or frozen. They need to manage this better and make sure the PC鈥檚 are continually serviced. No pads or pencils near the PC鈥檚 as a convenience to guests. Intangibles 鈥?Overall, service was impersonal if not indifferent. High points go to excellent Concierge staff, and very efficient and friendly bell-door staff. Front desk check in was OK and business like. One word of advice, the hotel does not do a good job at maintaining commitments. I had reserved my rooms far in advance and secured with credit card. Upon arrival they told me all rooms in my category were sold out and instead of correcting this, they downgraded me to a superior room and expected me to be satisfied with that. After some more complaining, I corrected this the next day when some executive rooms opened up. Again, this is an example of poor service quality on behalf of the reception desk. One of the days got colder in Hong Kong and the hotel didn鈥檛 turn on the heat. I turned up the room thermostat but it had no effect, the room got cold in the evening. Even in the hotel restaurant, I noticed the waiter had a watery nose due to the cold. Another example of the hotel鈥檚 failure to put the guests comfort first. What I鈥檝e just presented is an unvarnished view of this property as a result of my experience and observations. There are better hotels in Kowloon and HK in this price class. You will find much larger rooms and nicer properties in the Intercontinental HK, Intercontinental Grand Stanford, Sheraton Nathan Road, the Shangri-La or Harbour Plaza for rates that are similar or slightly more. Only thing the place has going for it is the relatively low room rates so for the budget minded traveler who won鈥檛 spend a lot of time in the room, the Langham Place would be fine bearing in mind this is not a true 5 star hotel when compared to some of HK鈥檚 great hotels. Location is a big negative, Tsim Sha Tsui or Central are much better location for the visitor-tourist. Mong-Kok is still rough around the edges. Not a lot of user-friendly (English speaking) restaurants in the neighborhood, you have to explore Central for dining options. Not worth the added travel and hassle to and from Mong Kok. Bottom line, would I return to the Langham Place for a repeat visit? Probably not.

<Author>donsyb
<Content>Fantastic Value For Money We booked this hotel because we got a great rate through BA when booking the flights.The hotel was great, service was fantastic. I had pre-ordered a bottle of wine for the room for my boyfriends 30th birthday, and a wonderful birthday cake was waiting for us in the room compliments of the hotel. The free drink on arrival was also a nice touch. It was Chinese New Year during our stay, and we were left Lai See packets, with chocoalte and biscuits in our room.We had the breakfast buffet a couple of times which had an exellent choice of both Chinese and international food, and ate there for dinner one night when the restaurant we wanted was full. Evening buffet was not as good as breakfast, and much more expensive, but still very good choice of food.It is only 15 minutes from Central by MTR, which we took mostly, (only used taxis to get to the Airport Express Station), as it was so cheap and efficient - even on the night of the New Year fireworks it only took us half an hour to get back, despite the thousands of people trying to do the same! The area around the hotel is authentically Chinese, which we loved, and we always felt safe as there were so many people around, even at night (due to the markets being open so late). It is only two minutes from Ladies Market, with so many bargains!I have only one complaint - check out was painfully slow, and had we used express checkout would have missed the 3 extra breakfasts someone had tried to book to our room!

<Author>jamieoliver
<Content>Langham Place and HK Disney My husband, 2 year old son and I just spent 5 days in Hong Kong from 21 to 25th of January. Langham Place Hotel, Mongkok: Not to be confused with Langham Hotel in Tsim Sha Tsui. We stayed 3 nights. It was conveniently located next to a train station. Although, if you are going on a short trip like us, it would have been better to stay in Tsim Sha Tsui, Causeway Bay or Hong Kong Central because the train trips do take up precious time. The hotel ambience is 5 stars but there are a few little annoyances which marred my impression. Toiletries were missing when we got there and not replenished daily. The cups were not cleaned properly after use. The desk was missing a lamp. The breakfast buffet ends far too early. 10am sharp. Tip- Don't pay for internet access in your room. Just use the free computers at THE PORTAL where you can borrow free dvds too. The other plus point is the free cot we got for our toddler.Hong Kong Disneyland: Best for kids under 8. Nothing much to offer teens and adults. Best to visit during cold season. Crowds were huge when we were there. Even on a weekday. Long queues. Watch out for unapologetic queue cutters. The Chinese Restaurant called Plaza Inn is yummy. Try the roast goose, soy chicken and sweetsour pork. The park was clean. Staff were polite but some ride attendants seemed jaded (already?!). Very disappointing that the park closed at 7pm on weekdays.We stayed one night at the HK Disneyland Hotel. Beautiful grounds. Good service. Sadly, many guests do not adhere to no smoking rule in common places. The kid's room service is good value. Fire alarm went off at 130am. It was disconcerting to see how unprepared the staff were in managing the event. Thankfully there was no real fire. Breakfast buffet was expensive but you have mickey, minnie, pluto, goofy walking around. Lotsa of photo opportunities. Tip: don't waste your time shopping in the park. The hotel shop has all the same things.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A Great Hotel- Can't wait to go back. I stayed at the Langham with a friend in November and it was a truly great experience. We had a twin executive room that had the most spectacular views. The rooms are well appointed and extremely comfortable. We received outstanding service during our 5 night stay, the staff at reception and particularly concierge provided excellent advice and were attentive and friendly. The hotel has the most amazing gym, pool and spa areas, I only wish we had more time to take advantage of these facilities. We did however manage to visit the lounge bar, one floor above reception, and enjoyed the happy hour 2 for 1 drinks and live music. The hotel is connected to a shopping complex and we found this convenient when we wanted a quick breakfast at Delifrance or Starbucks. Mongkok is an excellent location, it has the ladies market, great shopping, and good local restaurants. The MRT and KCR stations are a short walk from the hotel and the cheapest and easiest way to get around. I would recommend the Langham to anyone looking for value for money, location and service, it is a great hotel.

<Author>xhjsx
<Content>When can I return? This hotel has it all: friendly service, stylish rooms, easy access to the rest of the city; lots of shopping; knowledgable concierge staff; chic bar with live entertainment. The place is easy. Very friendly with no hassles. The breakfast buffet is situated in an elegant, tiered room and offers a large variety of chinese, japanese and western foods. You can have dim sum, freshly prepared omelets, a variety of very fresh pastries and fruits, miso soup, smoked salmon. It goes on and on. Step outside and you're in the middle of Chinese Hong Kong (Kowloon). Next door you can purchase Armani or Gucci and two blocks away you're in an open air clothing market. (Beautiful silk robes and jackets for about $25, jeweled clutches for $10. etc) Next door, under the mall, is the ultra modern subway. Two or three stops and you're most anywhere. The rooms are international modern, but small. The layout and mirrors make it seem larger, but if you and yours are large people, you might check out a suite. Otherwise they are very comfortable. Huge plasma screen on the wall. Space age bathroom. Real nice package. Enjoy.

<Author>broccolibaby
<Content>Fantastic Hotel in 'Chinatown' My fiance and I stayed at the Langham Place for 3 nights in April this year en route to Australia. The hotel was only open 2 months when I discovered it so there were few reviews to go on at the time, but the whole concept of the integrated hotel, office building and a shopping centre with 300+ shops in an authentic area of Hong Kong sounded intriguing, so I wanted to experience first hand for myself. We got a great deal too at 鈧?20 per room per night!We took the hotel bus from the airport to the hotel (only 鈧?2 each, one-way) and were greeted by several doormen and taken upstairs to the large reception area, which looks just like it did in the pictures - lots of mirrors, flowers and dark woods. There was a pianist and singer in the bar upstairs and you could hear them in reception - so first impressions were very good. The room was gorgeous - very comfy king bed, softest sheets, plasma screen  dvd, marble bathroom with seperate glass shower and contemporary furnished. I took a couple of dips in the bath and was nice to relax and watch the tv from the bath! And the view - couldn't have asked for anything better. We were only in a standard room (well that's what we booked anyway!) on the 18th floor but we'd views back towards the city, glimpses of the sea through buildings and below was the curved roof of the shopping centre. Especially pretty view at night.We arrived from London in the evening and we were pretty tired from the flight so we ended up eating in the hotel restaurant the first night and I had my first experience of many with chopsticks! I didn't want to be awkward and ask for cutlery so I just got stuck in! Food was fantastic, very pleasant staff and calm atmosphere - prices very reasonable for a hotel restaurant too (only 鈧?0 for 2 starters, 2 main courses, glass of wine and a beer!).The hotel is only a couple of minutes walk from Mongkok MTR station or Nathan Road and lots of buses but it is about 3km to the Star Ferry for example, at the southern tip of Kowloon. Although we walked from Kowloon a couple of times the hotel's location is a bit far for a 1 or 2 night stay or if you want to be in walking distance of everything. The area around the hotel is full of culture - and you actually feel like you're in China, rather than another big Asian/Westernised city, so I would say the hotel is luxury surrounded by culture.When we booked the pool was supposed to open in early April (we arrived 9th) but unfortunately it wasn't open and looked like it would still be a while due to set backs on sealing the pool. That was very disappointing but most of us know only too well construction rarely goes to plan. The spa looked heaven but we were saving for a Balinese massage in Bali!Free internet access in the hotel was very handy as we were able to send emails  webtexts home to say we arrived on the first leg of our journey safely and rub in how the great the place was! There is also a facility to borrow dvds free of charge.We didn't opt for breakfast but as some other reviewers mentioned there is a delifrance and another very good cafe on the otherside of the glass walkway that connects the hotel and shopping centre. You can even eat out on the balcony and look down on the activity below. Oh I should also mention our leaving experience! We only had a few HK$ left so rather than change some money we decided to experience a bit of local life and take one of the many buses (I've never seen so many buses in the one place anywhere in the world before!) back to the airport. The concierge offered to help us bring our bags to the bus stop!!! It was such a kind offer but we would have felt so stupid arriving at the bus stop with the suited out doorman that we gratefully declined - but it just showed how good the staff were. The concierge also advised on a very good local restaurant and our return airport bus!I would undoubtably stay here again, although as I said for a very short stay, you may prefer to be in a more convenient location in Tsim Sha Tsui or on Hong Kong Island.

<Author>Chuck, Santa Cruz
<Content>Affordable Five Star Hotel My wife and I stayed at the Langham in mid-October, 2005, so that I could attend the Hong Kong Electronics Fair. Due to the influx of visitors caused by the show, many hotels were booked and had jacked up their prices. We were able to stay at the Langham for an average of $250 per night, including taxes, which is an unbelievable deal for a hotel of this class.We had no problems with the room, the breakfast buffet, check-in/check-out, etc. An interesting feature is the 4th floor connection to the massive (12 story) Langham Place Mall which is across the street. This impressive shopping and restaurant mall has fascinating architecture, and a wide range of shops and eateries.Mong Kok is a little rough, probably known more for where the Hong Kong residents shop that a touristy place. There are apparently Saunas in the area where mischief takes place, but the streets feel relatively safe, and the MTR (subway) is located virtually in the basement of the adjacent mall.While not quite as convenient as the waterfront area of Kowloon, and without the famous view of the Hong Kong skyline, it's a tremendous value for a 4.5 star hotel. It's also close to the Mong Kok KCR (train) station, with easy access to the New Territories and Shenzhen.Susan and I highly recommend the Langham Place as an alternative to the conventional HK and Kowloon hotels.

<Author>gggggggg
<Content>Fantastic Hotel, great position My husband and I stayed at the Langham Place in Mongkok 23 Sept for 4 nights. I was a bit hesitant at being in Mongkok but am now convinced it is the best place to stay. It is one small block down from Nathan Rd. The rooms are a touch small but that is usual for HK and was quite manageable. The staff were very friendly and helpful at all times. We were actually upgraded to a suite as our window started leaking water (leftover from the heavy typhoon). If you would prefer not to pay for a full breakfast, try the Delifrance literally next door to the hotel, through the overhead pass. The breakfasts are cheap and the baguettes always amazing. For those Aussies, don't forget to pack your vegemite! The hotel's internet facilities were brilliant. They have 8 computers, a mixture of mac and pc all high speed and free to use any time. The adjacent shopping centre (Langham) is fantastic. If you are looking for young, hip original designers go to the ozone and spiral levels, very inexpensive. Go and look at Muji there, is fantastic. The food court is also good at the bottom of Langham shopping centre, good sushi, etc.

<Author>gromek
<Content>A wonderful experience! My fiancee and I stayed at the Langham Place Hotel in the vibrant part of Hong Kong called Mongkok. We stayed at the end of June-beginning of July which is part of the low season in Hong Kong. The hotel is brand new and a more or less integrated part of a huge new shopping complex (connected to it by an airbridge). The shopping mall itself is pretty cool with twisted walkpaths and very different than an average shopping mall. Mongkok is great! I had been there once earlier but not for more than a few hours making it hard to notice anything else than how busy it was. This time I had more time and it really is a very exciting and alive place! Lot's of food and lots of shops, and lots and lots of people! :) A few famous markets here as well! The temple street market is just outside the hotel - so is the Metro Subway so it's very convenient! The shopping mall has several cinemas and an abundance of restaurants (although we prefered to eat at the hotel or in the street restaurants)The hotel had a mouthwatering chocolate buffet! :)The hotel itself was such a great experience! I've travelled extensively all over the world and this is one of the nicest hotels I've stayed in for the price (it was low season). Since we are young people and very interested in Fitness I was suprised to find a fully equipped gym on the top floor, complete with a well educated english speaking personal trainer (free) and view over the entire hong kong. The gym was more hitech and better equipped than the small gym I use at home in Denmark. The top floor also has a spa facility where I had a fantastic 60min massage preparing me for the long flight home. They also serve free tea here in the lounge.Since we stayed in a suite on the club floor it's hard to say how the standard rooms are. I would imagine they are more spacious than other Hong Kong hotels (usually shoebox size). The older Eaton hotel by the same group has good sized standard rooms.We had booked the Junior suite but got upgraded to the Langham Suite upon arrival. This was one of the top 5 floors with amazing views from top to floor windows, a full kitchen (And I mean really there was everything, oven, microwave etc). The kitchen was very modern and all in stainless steal. We had two 42 plasma screens, one in the bedroom and one in the living room. The bathroom was huge with a seperate shower cabin and seperate bathtub. A huge glass wall seperate the bedroom from the bathroom which is quite fun. Obviously there's a button you can press and an automatic white wall comes down so you have privacy. It has to be seen. The club lounge has full breakfast and snack for lunch and dinner. We easily got full on the snacks which are pretty much a meal. They had great chocolate cookies :) . Service was flawless. We went out one day and asked for a champagne cooler and glasses to be put up after 2 hours exact. When we came back from the winestore (often cheaper than the supermarket for champagne) the cooler was ready and full of ice. So we cooked a nice dinner ourselves and set a table up next to the huge window, put on a cd on the all room music system, dimmed the lights and had dinner and champagne with the greatest view in Hong Kong. The club lounge have a free selection of new DVD movies and cds that you can borrow to the room. We had a fantastic stay and we are diffinitely coming back! Also happily in a non suite room! ;)
